O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the summary of medicine's knowledge at its end, and finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I saw in my vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of manual skills, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is practiced in our region and is everywhere unknown, so it has been lost and its knowledge has been taken away, and nothing remains from it beyond the small descriptions in books by the ancients that were handled by the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and closed minds, and science has been moved away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems I should revitalize this treatise altogether according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will follow together the forms of the cautery instruments and other tools for use with their adjustment and preparation, just as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters are found in our time for this reason, the art of medicine has been extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who interferes to master in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until they know the location of the limbs and their shapes and connections and separations, and have knowledge about bones, nerves and arteries, and the number of bones, and their movement and rest positions, and where their exit lies.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus says Hippocrates that rest with rest is much, and work with work is little; and similarly in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone is not aware of what has been said before, they might commit errors and waste others' time; just as I have seen many times more than once with those who interfere in this science and abandon their knowledge and lack of experimentation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who amputated one of the neck ulcers or a woman's goiter, and cut into her arteries around the neck; because so much blood came out that the woman died in her surgeon's hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in an elderly man, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to remove it, and saw the position of the wound and the size of the stone, and indeed if they operated on him he died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw one other case which was treated by draining Duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breakage there was an injury; and the patients were full of ignorance causing the break to occur in the wound from being treated roughly, and did not allow any healing at all for the injury, and did this until one month; and he was commanded not to move it again; so he stayed like that until his leg was completely swollen and his feet, and resulted in ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to relieve the leg; and when I heard it being dislocated so smoothly that he did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the corruption was already established or throughout a member, and could not be cured; and the corruption did not cease to spread within the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see a second wound that collapsed an abscess in a crooked way, and then inflamed due to the mischief of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a gangrene, when it is of dark bile humor, one should not touch it with iron if it is in its place so that all the corrupted parts can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear children, you need to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: that is to say, one where there is danger in multiple dispositions; and I will show you in each section of this book where it has power and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because it is necessary that you guard yourselves, so that no one can say ill of you. If you take up your weapons in caution and act gently but firmly on your illnesses, use the best method so that through God's grace you come to salvation and be blessed; and leave unending sorrows of sickness behind. And remove from those who cause you doubt, have faith in yourself so that you may go from this world to glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen instructs in some of his admonishments: "Do not take any illness as a remedy that you might be called foolish by others.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters deal with fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and the chapters are organized from the head down to stones; and about the shapes of instruments, and the metals for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the operation.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters concern cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar matters; and these chapters are organized with descriptions of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters; and they are arranged from the head down to stones, and include descriptions of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we remember from the work, it is necessary for me to discuss the quality of each remedy and its harm associated with each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I state that the qualities of assistance, and the harm, are the longest word and subtlest science and the secrets respond. And many wise people spoke about this, agreeing with it; and they satisfy me with their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I state that the cautery helps universally for any complexion where there is matter, because there are two kinds of complexions: this means hot complexion with substance and dry complexion with substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry complexion combined with matter, they divided their thoughts and said that the cautery is a great aid. And the other group said the opposite: that the cautery only helps in diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot and should not be treated with hot illnesses by heat or drying. And it contradicts those who say otherwise, that the cautery provides great assistance to hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of people.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the nature of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion by experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And for all procedures, do not interfere except that which has been proven and by long use is known the chapter of cautery, and the variety of human complexion, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and time period; we have no fear from other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the parts should assemble and align with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know this, my children, that assembling a fire-based cautery contains secrets of healing and yields even greater goodness than a burning medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth from any member that is cooked, and does not harm another member if it's not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot medicines move from one part to another and bring about diseases of sickness elimination in the body; and by chance they can cause maladies. The fire, due to its potency and quality, does not do this unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experimentation and the length of my service and study in the art, it aligns with the truth of things; and because of this, I apologize for the length of speech, as I do not wish to withhold from you the secret of fire and its quality, how it removes diseases from bodies, as the philosopher explains when demonstrating. Receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, boy, that they decided when the cauterizations should be done, and read prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, because the harms arising are most removed by the help of the cautery; and likewise if the cauterizations are for necessary pains that cannot wait until greater evil befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like those foolish people, child; for there is no recurrence to a disease cured by cauterization. They say it this way: but they are mistaken, because cauterizations are only medicine that changes the complexion and dries out the fluids causing pain, which is more effective than medicine for hastening recovery, and due to the power and authority of its work.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the possibility is that the disease does not return at all according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness and its effects; they are gathered together in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things. If no cauterizations are administered or if there's little excess and moisture, as with cauterizations for pain, and similar conditions, then this kind of pain does not return again; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And not many people understand why cauterizations are named the last of medicine, and this can be seen; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine. But their understanding is false, and they say cauterization is the last of medicine because when our methods for cures in any disease do not work, then we administer our cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Thus clearly cauterizations are the last of medicine, not according to the understanding of those who say otherwise.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauterizations are more effective than iron ones and they stated this because of the quality of gold and its high substance. They also mentioned that the skin under iron cauterizations does not rot; however, it's not true as I've proven it myself and found that in some individuals, it can indeed happen. Gold cauterizations are better than iron ones, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat the gold tool, you do not realize that it is heated by the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down; and if you heat it too much; then put it in fire; thus, there is enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our metal cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So I have organized this chapter about the shoulder joint up to the elbow, so that one may find it more easily.
dou cautere olivaire	oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The fire cautery works with moisture and cold on the brain. There are two ways to do it due to an illness called 'soda', and due to many fluids that descend from the head as sweat, from ears, and because of multiple dreams and toothache, throat pain, and especially for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is cleansed by a dissolving medicine altering the head. Three or four times, or five times according to how well the powers and the strength and the habit of the patient can bear it; and then wash off the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place his hands between yours and put your hands under his nose. After that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two nostrils; and let it come where your middle fingers are, if blood is drawn out, then heat up the cautery which is called 'olivare', from which here is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the joint in its natural position with ink, and guide your hand downwards and sideways gradually and steadily while turning it; then lift your hand alone, and check if you see bone. If you don't see any bone, continue with the cautery until you do see bone as I have instructed; after that take one pinch of sand, put a moistened cotton inside and place it in the joint, allowing it to be there for three days; afterwards apply a butter on top of a cloth; leave it on until the scorching disappears; then treat the wound with the ointment known as 'tetrafarmaçon', continuing until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they said that the older ones believed, when a wound stays open longer, more pus discharges out; and because of this advice moves.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And it was said by none of them that we should let the cautery burn for so long that part of the bone becomes ashes, and then one must set back what has been burnt from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say the other that we must let the cautery burn there and press so hard that it raises as wide like a small egg that women place in their bellies because fluids can be expelled out of it; and should we leave the wound open for a long time afterwards; after this, we should clean it and dress it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of using a cautery do not seem to me to be good in every respect, except when it comes to certain patients with fear; and I believe that I should leave them alone; because the joints become weakened by continuous exposure to nature's fluids, as we demonstrate with other limbs; and even when the joints are weak from nature itself, and my first experience of using a cautery is more healing and soothing for me, and in doing so I gather together salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the old head pain
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the entire head comes chronic pain that lasts for a long time, one should use the patient's fingers and pills which are called "cochies," and also do cleansing of the head and ears with bandages; and if one performs the cautery as we have previously mentioned to them, then it proves effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the shoulder of the patient is of strong nature and not too cold; therefore, apply the cautery slightly over the part where we previously mentioned to do so.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After apply the cautery to each horn of the head up to the bone, just as we have said previously, and perform one application of it over where it is called "vessel"; and make one application of it in the place where suction cups are placed; and lighten your hand so that you do not go beyond the bone: patients feel more intense pain with this cautery than others, and I will discuss this further elsewhere; and it should be noted that the applications to the horns should be subtler than that used for the middle part of the head, and it's the form:
dou cautere dou chief	A fire cautery, for the purpose of a patient, instructs them to let their hair grow long and even; and if it starts pricking at its base when they are young, one should hold steady so as not to move until they fully grow.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When pain suddenly comes to a part of the head and extends till to the eye, and if the shoulder is purged by mild medicines, and other treatments I mentioned about diseases have been done in the division of diseases, but none of them help: then one should do cautery according to two ways, meaning with medicine water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine water cauteries involve you taking a spoonful of oil, and then applying the bark and dressing to two pieces each for both shoulders, in such a way that you can place the spoonful of oil on the skin; and when it is placed, ensure it adheres well and leaves it like this for 12 hours. Then remove and treat with garlic butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the oil cure until it is healed; and if you see that doing some of those burning medicines that I have written or the first treatment of burning medicines works for you.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery should be done like this.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which I have described:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc. de emigraine	From headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre. de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have instructed in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you apply cautery to them according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in a healthy position; and cut the hair on his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shift his head; after this, apply moistened cotton inside an egg or garlic juice to the eye; then heat the cautery which is prepared: and place it close to the head as if it were a feather of a rooster, so that the tip of the cautery rests there; if you see it, let the tip point from one part of the head to another, and if you can see it, let it be like a tent; but in any case, it is better for your work that it not move.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, and treat any pus, then dry it off; and if it is closed, operate on it, remove from the bowe; afterwards place the heated cautery in this manner, hold your hand near the cautery to the part below the eye, so that your hand does not cause trouble; and put the cautery into the oil grease, and let it fume.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then restart the cautery one more time, and if you need it again, let it rest for three days. Afterwards, place wet cotton on butter, and continue with the ointment cure until healed. When forty days have passed without healing, apply corrosive water medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow this regimen according to what your chapter recommends.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method for cauterizing fistulas that none of the old ones mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand by "fistula", and make it clean; after that, place the thin camel bone inside the cut:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they do it in the size of three parts of a spoon; and hold your hand or camel firmly, making sure not to move the patient's skin so that the melted wax does not drip onto their eye; and one should put moistened cotton on the eye before applying an egg yolk or oil: the wax then removes the pus from the boil, and through marvelous healing, it saves health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through cauterization as we have described, that's good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer pertussis to the child, and return the fistula to the body within the child according to what should be done in its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of cuts in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cuts appear on the lips that are referred to as 'whiskers', and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When treating these cuts using what we've discussed in sections, and if the treatment doesn't help, then use this method: apply a small surgical instrument for cauterization like this:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place him quickly in those openings until they grow; afterwards, clean the wound where it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil on the neck
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or on the gland, or at the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it turns rotten and swells up and becomes discolored, turning into a fistula; then you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not heal: so you need one cautery according to the size of the fistula; after removing the pus from the fistula, keep your hand until the iron tip reaches the bottom and beyond the lesion; do this process once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is healthy; if it heals like this, it's good; and if not, you need to uncover the area and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in your medical text.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened due to moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it through medicines and that doesn't help, then place the head of the patient on your healthy side; afterwards heat up the cautery according to which will come after in this manner: that you put a twig onto the tooth; and place inside the cautery quickly burning hot, hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and restart the cautery according to your desire; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and leave it there for an hour and then remove it.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the moving teeth are stabilized, and the softened gums are restrained, and the moisture is corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	from toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from coldness, or there's coldness or ice present, and medical remedies don't help, then one must use cauterization according to two methods: and the wax cautery and the fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Wax cautery if it's like this: you take butter from a cow, and at the tip of a metal or iron spoon; after that take cotton and wrap it on the point of a needle, and moisten the cotton with melted butter, then put it quickly over the painful tooth and hold until it cools down; and do this often until its effectiveness reaches to the root of the tooth. And if you see cold hair and cotton moistened in cooled butter, apply it again onto the painful tooth, and place a hot iron on it until heat from the fire reaches to the nerve of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Assemble a fire cautery as you desire, using something like a hot iron or needle, and make it large enough so that the heat doesn't enter the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, from which the form will come afterwards, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be relieved that day or the following.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter in anticipation of this hot cautery, and then immediately apply it. And this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery to the extent that you wish it, and according to what is within your ability; this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	regarding the instructions for dealing with scrophula (also known as King's Evil or leprosy).
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophula is due to cold humors and not responsive to treatment with medicines, then heat the cautery as described later in this text, and make two openings for fumes to escape from the other side of the cautery; and place the heated cautery over the abscess once or twice as needed until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, adjust the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it in this position for three days; and cover with wet cotton saturated in butter until the pus is drained; afterwards cleanse the area with ointments and swabs until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of sugar:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the humors conquer in the channels of the lungs, and especially when it comes from cold constitution, then it is necessary that the body be cleansed first with diuretic medicines; afterwards make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to come all the way to the throat, but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After I make another cautery at the joint of the neck and head of the spinous process, let it be known that this type of cautery is called "clavile," as we have before us its form; and treat the area in such a manner as previously described until it heals properly.
de la toust	To the cautery of fire, command the sick to let their hair grow long and even; and if they stick at their root, hold the eyes firmly so they do not move until they grow.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	For all and every disease of the lungs are due to cold moisture, and the patients do not have fever nor chills, and they are diseases that come from old age, then you should apply two cauteries on their force (or strength) in their veins; and one other cautery right under the buttocks between the breasts. And let the cautery called 'clavile' be the one according to the form which was mentioned previously.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, perform the cautery by applying force to all of the cautery known as "pox," as its form is described above in the illness of the ears; and let there be 30 pox marks, or more, depending.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After curing the area as described previously, and for this type of treatment, let there be three rounds of cautery following this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for this reason are the cauteries lighter, because you make them three times over.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture and it is set back in place, then it cannot stay put; instead, it immediately dislocates again with small movements as we have experienced. Thus, it befits you to first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After that, bind the wounds on his back and sides; then remove the kidney inside the scrotum with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, heat the cautery to just two fingers' width as described here for this process:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	And cauterize the palm up to its knuckle, and let the mark of the cauterization come together in one point. Four cauterizations; and for this reason, perform the cauterization using the tool with three prongs, because it is due to the intricacy of a tent that there are four marks resulting from cauterization; and the nerves follow along like threads and the form of the cauterization tool with three prongs:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And each time, fix it on this one nerve because there are seven cauterizations for it.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After placing the fire cauterizer over the nails, grind with a thong; after that, rest the patient, and do not let any of the limbs be in long tension until it is well stabilized.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it was relieved above, resulting in little else, then perform a cautery on the thickness of the clavicle cautery, or use slightly more cautery force.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the injuries to the patient are healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and moisture affect the stomach in proportion to its nature, they multiply the catharsis within it, and follow established treatment methods which do not benefit him. Therefore, it is necessary for the patient's injuries to be bandaged on their back, and stretch out their legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From this onwards, apply three fire cauterizations below the heel on the buttocks for a quantity equivalent to that of two. For every cauterization, target the clavicle, and two cauterizations behind each pair of ribs until the pattern of cauterizations forms at three angles, ensuring space between them so they do not join together when subjected to corruption; ensure that all cauterizations thoroughly burn both sides of the knee, and form this shape without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see it cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach like this form; and whoever fears from that cautery, cauterize by pressing and judging on the stomach at one point according to the quantity you see of it; then cauterize completely through the entire cautery which is called 'points'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have administered, as long as it's clean.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, it causes pain in the chest and due to moisture and excessive wind. It must be treated through its natural complexion by getting rid of excess. The body will not benefit from this treatment if the liver is soothed on top of its bile ducts; and three cauterizations should be performed according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, beyond the lateral aspects, where bile comes out; leave a space between each cautery about twice the size of a coin; and let the cauterization cover both the long and short sides without pressing your hand down fully over the whole area; only burn half the kidneys and have the body in place under its feet; if it can't do this, let it lie down, stretch its legs, and lift its arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to do so, cauterize these fire cauteries using a knife, be subtle and skilled in this art, and guard that you do not burn all the flesh, for you would dry out the whole body; and let it only boil up until a point, because the flesh is very delicate at that spot, and know how to see it.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has moved to the liver, and you know whether it is within the liver tissue or on the surface: if it's within the tissue, the patient feels pain but not excessively strong; and if it's on the surface, they feel intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment brings the disease to its head, it is necessary for the patient's body to surround its head; and then mark out where the disease has spread on the body, and then heat up the cautery that resembles a needle, as you see here is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And apply the cautery until the knees are charred, and continue till the scabs are all gone; after this heal according to wound treatment until it is healed; and one must not use this cautery anywhere else than those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, because these hands caused no diseases ever.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can safely operate, and every time it seems to me that movement is better than leaving it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the water cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The old ones said that one should make water cauteries of the roots of aristologe, and do it like this: take a long root of aristologe, the longest you can find, let it be dry, and also as big and as long as your hands; then soak it in oil, heat it up on fire, and apply the cautery between your shoulders and neck for one application, and two small applications lower down where is below the chin; and four applications between the fifth and sixth rib, going slightly behind; and one application near the belly button, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and four more at the ribs towards the end of the application that's between the two shoulders; don't squeeze your hand, instead do it openly as when you smell.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And it is said by no old man that any person uses a fire cautery like shaving at the neck, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs, until it reaches this abscess; and then the pain leaves, as we have described for the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this chapter is fear or that the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of the mice in those ways we have discussed for wound treatments, and it doesn't benefit, then they try three methods of cautery that are all good.

After I place the two heated needles on each other until they pierce from the other side, and then remove the cautery, in this way it will remain for four. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has taken forrot (or decay) over a long period, and this is as effective as all other previously mentioned cures.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery isn't suitable for indigo (or certain materials), except when it's done in the way that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment doesn't help, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations inside the mouth, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the kidneys, and one behind the back on the spine, and one place at the anus; and make sure that the cauterizations are well close to the spine near the kidney.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery in place for a long time to treat gangrene, do not stop treating the patient after the cautery treatment; and then recovery would speed up, and all four intentions would be fulfilled with God's help.

de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back

Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see this, apply the cautery between two or three lines on the spine with the burning tip of the cautery, making sure the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment is done as long as it remains clean according to what we have said, and be cautious not to apply the cautery in places of weakness where nerves are located.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture spreading to every limb, and when the pain comes from the feet, which people call "gout" properly, and when it's due to cold reasons and cannot be cured with medicines, such can be treated with cauterizations in this manner: make the animal of cauterizations near the joint on the foot, and let the cauterizations be olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it needs that you apply the heat on the abdomen below the foot, if you cause a burn over the entire area where we claim 'point'.

And if the pains extend to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, if you have to apply heat on each knee three or four olive oil burns; and if needed more, do so, but don't remove your hand until the wound is thoroughly burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knees and back, then one should apply the cautery as we have described in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are at the hands, make points in the armpit area II lines; and if there remains any pain in the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and apply remedies.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if you give them good care and cleanse phlegm, they will recover with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of the uterus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture occurs in the stomach and the intestines fall into the cervices (birth canal), this is new. It is necessary that when you see it being cured, do not remove it during day; and use things that relieve the belly, so that the insides descend from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to rub his anus until the intestines are repaired, then take them with your fingers, and pinch just under the rupture onto the bone of the knee, and have it look as if there is a sign halfway up the front, like half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery to its form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and emits pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz. Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach to the bone with the cautery, your operations are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and likewise large people should have large ones according to their size. Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, have him wear a well-made bandage and keep it on for another forty days; and have good rest, so that he doesn't overwork himself and avoids overeating or drinking too much, and avoid too loud shouting; and once he follows this advice, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall say about after the practice of cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come to other abdomens and are visible, and you notice they no longer grow, then apply the fire cautery according to its quantity, and use one-third of the full measure; after treating them as we have said; and none of the old ones advised that one should cauterize with the cautery at three angles according to this form:

de meselerie	In amalgamation
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The mire is helped once by each cautery with great assistance, and similarly the disease that comes from the putrefaction of blood and melancholy.

And never is a cautery done with the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus such flesh is removed; and always no one should intervene if it isn't someone knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	From balms

When the disease known as "albaras" progresses and medicine in the form of remedies proves ineffective, then apply heat from a cautery slightly over its surface, according to the thickness of the blood found there, until the pus is removed and the color changes; then clean with flour mixed with lentils and rose oil, plantain leaves, and blood from a sheepdog and an almond, each in their respective parts; mix all together, wrap it with a cloth, and leave on that part until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for the chancre by cautery

Another way of disease is called 'corrodens', and it's no other thing than a member ailment, for it consumes limbs as if they were dry twigs.

des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The text discusses conditions that come with stones.

Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	The fire cautery requires that you heat it up to the point where it becomes as hot as a goose feather, and it should be made of strong iron at a size that can capture nails from all directions, with delicate margins. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with ointment, ensuring it is not applied when it's dirty.

li cure dou trembler	He heals by shaking

quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.
