Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless, whenever this happens to no one, if you hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein and hold it as tightly as possible until his pulse is calmed under your finger, and that no more drops come out; then light several small and large olive oil cauteries until they are all red. Then take one or many according to the size of the wound and apply them where the artery was running, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until his pulse is fully restored.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, then quickly take another one of the cauterizing instruments that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to perform this one after the other until the tooth becomes black; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve which is beneath, and that no harm comes upon the patient; and know that when the tooth comes out of the artery, it cannot remain well even if the artery is large, unless this is done through one of these four methods that we have mentioned: by cautery, by extraction if it has not been treated already, by strong string tying, or by medicines placed upon it which have the power to harden blood; and let it be tied and restrained in due course.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer hardening through tightly binding with cloths or placing things that burn upon it, or similar actions, if they do not benefit in this way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no means or medicine at hand, so they should place their index on the wound of the artery in the manner that we have said, and stretch it well until the area above the wound and above the artery is hardened; and do not move the finger but dampen it with cold water often as much as can be cold until the tooth becomes frozen and swollen and hardened. And prepare for cautery and medicines for what needs them.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for surgery
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all about every disease for which it is necessary to apply a fire cautery, or medicine that heats up, and we discussed their uses, causes, instruments, and forms of application; and I put that chapter dealing with the head until the feet, and now I will proceed in this chapter along the same route as those things are found more easily for what you want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this one, it is necessary for you to know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first book about cautery, so here greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	And none of the ways of people come to treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who suffered so much with their illness that they died lightly due to the foolishness they found in their sickness, and the great suffering of their disease; and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there is someone who gives their insight and says: "Wait, I am brave"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting for you to agree with those who come to you in this manner, but place greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not hastily but wisely rely on what you are certain of and can know; and use prediction and indication in your treatments where health has been converted; and this will help you gain good reputation, glory, and enduring memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of their hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have instructed you this chapter by discussing chapter by chapter, according to what is before or the chapter on cauteries, which I discussed from head to heel, because you will find it easier for that which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of water at its head
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this sickness comes very often to children at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the head of the child; and it happens none other time because of some reason that cannot be identified.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this sickness happen outside of children, and among all those that I have seen, their death came quickly; and because of this, it seems to me that I should abandon the practice of this disease with such remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child of these, his shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day so much that it could not bear anymore; and he thought it to be too much moisture until he died, and this moisture is assembled right over the bone under the siphon, between the heart and the bone; and the veins are like this when the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and abscesses are small that you cut through the head a wide crack; and it's as long as two fingers, as long as the moisture flows; and see here the shape of the spathile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more extensive, and the abscesses are larger, make two cuts in the manner of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the symptoms you see are that the corners of the head open on each side, and the water jumps when you press it from your hand inside, and this does not respond to treatment: then it is necessary that you make three cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after making an incision, remove all moisture completely outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the incisions of bandages and powders, and then applying wine and oil, leave it like this for up to five days; then remove the dressing, treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and allow the head to heal evenly. Finally, let the patient eat dry meat from a source that is free of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look at where the large opening of the abscess is, and the assembly of the water; for it is not always in front; nor always behind; neither always on the right; nor always on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut accordingly where the abscess opens and the water filling it, making the incision according to what you can do, and watch that you do not cut the artery; let a flow of blood, so that the patient dies due to the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of cautery by fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it comes to any illness that is called "catarrh" affecting the eyes or at the bottom of them, and this sickness is ancient, and the medicine cure doesn't help, then the last resort treatment if is the cautery with which one cuts off the two main arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you can see your patients again, have them take off their headwear; after that, rub the scalp with a coarse cloth until veins are visible. Then remove the patient's neck collar to accommodate all one piece of cloth; then observe where the pulse is taken, and examine both sides up to the ears, noting if they were previously pulsating; then mark their temples with chalk, then cover each side with a sharp cut from two parts, cutting until the bone is visible. This should be done considering the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, clamp the spatula over the artery and above it, cut also like two thumbs through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, make the patient jump from above continuously outwardly.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to touch it, you should measure out the space of three fingers. Then press and push until you reach the bone; that is where one must remove six cosses, plus or minus a bit according to how the patient can tolerate it and the reformation of the artery. Afterward, inspect the wound: if there remains any part on the bone close to the syphacus [a specific medical term], and if the pus-filled abscess has not emerged from the opening you just made then compress the wound site, seal it up, apply ointment until fully healed.
de emigrainne	From sanding
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old age comes and severe congestion occurs, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and ears that have been known for a long time and similar things. Medicine treatments are done using methods of medical cure and nothing of this benefits it. We extract the arteries in the temples and apply cauterization, as we have detailed.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient sweats after their head hair, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well due to its pulsation, and responds only in some who are too cold; if she responds, then pull the neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and warm water until the artery becomes visibly apparent; then take the sponge tool as described:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then slightly scrape the skin until you feel the artery, then pull it up with forceps and make sure to remove all of the tissues that are in the area from each part; if the artery is thin, then cut it at the tip of the little finger, after which take out and discard the parts corresponding to those two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it isn't cut, neither will escape all pain completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat bleeding for two days and nights. And if the artery is large, you must bind it with two thicknesses of a strong silk thread for two days before, so that infection does not occur during wound healing and to prevent blood loss; then remove excess between the two threads at that same moment. If possible, apply the cut cautery up to the bone as long as the shoulder is cut; this is the surgical procedure if the patient doesn't have fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterization helps to finish off moisture issues: because this is more effective against moisture compared to other methods.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one must fill the wound with old cotton and place well-made wicks on top; and when they are removed, they should be treated with dried medicines that produce pus, and wicks, until cleanliness occurs; and if there is no artery to cut from them, you proceed as you would normally, then hurry to apply cauterization, or use the space of vitriol and tighten it in your hand so that the artery becomes hard. And if you don't have this available, you can place water on top until the artery freezes, and lift the cold water over it until it stops bleeding and is tightened as necessary; and the one that is softer and easier to extract from an artery should be cauterized with this cutting cautery across two parts, but make sure the cuts are well spaced to retain heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less of their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And should have between the two knives an inch of space, and then when you are ready to apply the two edges, place the hot iron until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places. And keep them separated by the two heads because there is no welding from this cautery across; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are draining from the veins that are located on the back of the head's neck, and medicine doesn't provide any benefit for this ailment, you notice the skin turning red due to it, and feel or see sweating on the forehead as if in a fever; and when they are damp and wet such that the paper hair falls off, and the papers become heated, burned by the heat of the tears, this is where one needs this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the old "healer of injuries", and when you apply this treatment to the patient with this disease, let them have hair or front. Then make three cuts evenly on their forehead according to its length; make one cut as wide as two doves across the forehead starting from below and moving upwards until it reaches the nose. The other two cuts should be two as two doves long over each eye, making sure not to incise any of the arteries that are located above the eyes. Keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws; make each wound three doves wide across; have a piece of sponge and some cloths ready to wipe off the blood, then use a sharp tool from two sides as shown here for this form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is below the temple up to the second incision; and peel off all the tissue in between the two cuts until you reach the membrane covering the bone, then continue cutting from the middle incision up to the other second cut, and then remove this pus.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you use the first opening tool which is called 'cultellaire', and it is very sharp on one side, while being blunt, not sharp, on the other side, and this tool has a shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And make the cut towards the inner flesh at the edge, and the bone cut towards the bone, and the blade until it feels at the half fracture.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And pierce all the vessels that descend from the head as veins until the cut is continuous up to this one opening at the edge, and then do another part along the middle fracture up to the other opening; and then extract the equal blood equally, and express the body with the blood taken; then place a piece of old cotton in each fracture, and put wet cloths covered with wine and oil and asphodel on them, and ensure that no pus appears; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply large quantities of water lilies, then take care with the ointment basilicon mixed with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	from the pus
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any sudden cough occurs habitually, and you see the eyes weak and small, and weakening of sight, and burned paper; and the hair falls out, and one sweats profusely from the forehead in a fever, and the patient experiences intermittent pain; then know through these incidents that those materials and that mucus come only from many veins, and the curative process underway is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient behind their forehead, then make a large incision along the forehead, and another one slightly wider than an inch below it.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Start from the temple on the left to the temple on the right with your incision, and let the cut go until it reaches the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move during eating. And when the bone is exposed, drain all the blood using a sponge. Then cleanse inside the wound between the two lips of the incision and put in old cotton, followed by linen. After that, cover with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil. Avoid cutting into anything unwanted; once it's taken out, you should rub the bone until cartilage begins to form, then clean it with desiccating substances, which encourage cartilage growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of the flower of wheat and four parts of colofon, and make a plaster from them; and administer it to these wounds to promote cartilage growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	regarding ear piercing
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that is found in the ears is one of the four things: grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, like beans, peas; or something discharging like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it comes to the hole in the ear or any other manner of thing that does not fit into the ear, nor grows within the ear, place the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if any violet oil or saffron oil drops out, then proceed with extraction; and have them inhale camphor, and block their nostrils when the inhalation comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and hold the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	This treatment often fails; and if it does not work, then proceed with needle extraction, as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it leaps out with the forceps, that's good; if not, proceed to extraction using a fine double curved needle; and if it doesn't leap out through this, make an arnica stick and pinch the tip of the stick or the ear's wick very hard, then plug the area around the wick with solid wax so that nothing can enter with the wick; then pull forcefully because many times it helps as we have said; and if it doesn't help in this manner either, take some glue from this and put a little tool to its point for doing this thing, and place a bit of cotton inside; then press the glue onto the stone or anything else, and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not allow these things that we have spoken about to take place, you must quickly pierce the ear in this manner so that pus and blood drain out, and muscle contractions follow. And the method for piercing is as follows: first prepare the patient with a cold application on the area of the head, then remove the blood according to the size of its strength, afterwards put the patient's head between your hands and turn the ear upwards, make a small cut in the root of the ear towards the fat that hangs down; and let the wound be like a crescent moon until you reach the bone. Then break the bone according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth; continue treatment as long as it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grains (probably referring to small infections or swellings) and they are present and cause swelling, you should administer an extraction; and if he cannot come out, then perform a fine incision according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And perform the incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this if you think the grains are wet due to the ear's moisture, until you have extracted many pieces; then remove them with fine needles and suction, as we said before, so that the extractions are gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In an ear infection, then when someone sneezes in the ear, it is necessary for patients to perform some preliminary coughing actions, and widen their ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let there be healing within that same ear where the infection is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out into heaven, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If heaven doesn't allow it, take many stones according to their size and gently. Warm them slightly on fire and put one or several inside the ear of the patient, and blow them out from another foot, and strike with another stone against the stone in the ear; continue this action of one stone after another until all the infection comes out entirely, then it will jump out completely; if you can see, take a bit of wood and put one piece of shoulder into the ear, the other touch with fire until the more tender part of the wood is burnt. Then redo different pieces of wood until the entire infection has come out, as we have said about stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of worms, if they are small like fleas and similar creatures, treat them as we have explained in the division; but if they can be felt due to their large size, then perform worm extraction using forceps; this is the easier thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of tangled worms in the ears, if you're applying treatments as we have described in division and using distillation methods, but no cure is effective, then it's necessary to observe the ear with sunlight: if there are no worms visible, use fine forceps for removal; if nothing is visible, take this form of cane here that corresponds.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And make it narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And place the finest needle in the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then puncture through the entire canal; do this repeatedly until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not want to come out, stuff the cotton wick in as I have said for stones in the ear canal; and if they do not penetrate like we have said, administer distilled liquids that the old ones tested in the treatment of worms, and you will find information on these distillations elsewhere; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with this device, as shown here is how you should proceed:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or lead, being narrow at the bottom for .i. small openings and wide above to distill from; and for pressing inside the distillation use a well-made tool of lead suitable for this purpose, and if you see take a blade and wrap it around the end with cotton; then pour your oil or juice onto the wick, and what you see of your medicines in the wick, and let the wick be in the ear; then press within the blade all the cotton, and press your hand properly until the oil is distilled or when the ear feels relieved; and feel inside the patient, and do one portion of heated distillation as if it's being distilled into the ear; and make sure it’s not too cold, because the medicine wouldn't be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	regarding ear piercing
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any part missing in their ears; and this same thing happens to people due to wound impact or a fetus being born inside the ear. And these impacts often happen within the ear if it cannot be seen; and it does not occur twice, so one can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, what comes inwardly, if one cannot see it, is due to grief in the process of healing from multiple conditions. And concerning this where we can see, you should put the ear close to the sunlight; and look inside: if you see the obvious pus, that which forms like this from the material within:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And do so and cut evenly in front and behind it all the way through, without hurting the ear; if the pus is from a fetus or a part of the ear, if you have subtle pincers, gently pinch it until that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the earwax is far in the ear, take a fine, light probe and heat it slightly on the flame, then insert it into the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you notice the inflammation of which the ears feel irritated in hearing, gently pierce it and ensure that you do not injure the nerves of the ear; then place a tent into the ear according to the size of its opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take an eardrum and stuff it with rose water ointment, and apply powdered vitriol. If you see swelling in the ear, you should remove the eardrum and replace it with another one that's moistened with a wick made of rose oil and beeswax, until all the swelling has disappeared; then treat it until it is clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a cloth and wring out cold water, then place it on the ear, and apply other treatments that stop bleeding, which include therapies involving distillation processes.
de la char des papieres	From the ashes of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	When dealing with hairs that come from the eyes when they are wet and then dry, it's necessary to spread them out with tweezers and forceps, and take off their roots with a pincers. Then, place sulfur in the area where the vinegar is applied.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are not peeled off, apply a fine lens cautery to them and do the cauterization after incision; and repeatedly check, because nothing remains of their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots burn and don't return.
de la gresle	From the ice block
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, in the sheets of parchment, there appear some things that seem to gleam with their form and texture, and because of this, it is called "hail" disease. This ailment is an assembly of large moisture on the surface and inside of the sheet; here are the actions: be cautious when the hail stays still from one side and another, and this is a simple thing to know; then cut it broadly, then lightly burn each part, afterwards pinch it, and scoop it out.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you can't cover it without piercing a bit of the paper, so long as it doesn't harm the patient; and if it tears greatly, stitch it together with one seam, and treat it until it is healed; and if it's small, don't apply force there, for the ointment will heal it quickly and promote new flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granule goes down inside the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper and there are granules on one forceps, extract and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it doesn't harm anything; and when the granules have been extracted, wash out with salty water, and cure the wound until the patient's healing progresses.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of granules
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that saturates the paper in its sheets; this happens more often with children than adults, and it doesn't harm their eyes much; they experience weeping catharre in the mornings, and cannot look at the sun's light because tears quickly accumulate in their eyes. Thus, they lie down in their diapers right away, sleep on them, and have their papers moist under their eyelashes; as a result, the Exinach appears and changes their appearance, spreading within the eye upon opening it.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the hand with your fingers and feel the exit between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of this treatment is such that the patient places their head in your healthy area. Then take one linen sheet and set up a tent in manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains extraction from each part, then place it; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the extraction be assembled within the circle. Then make a cut through the wetness in the middle of the moist area, creating an opening of the length, not more than the wound as we do for cutting a vein; and make the leather fit perfectly until you see the extraction through it; and in various arrangements comes out the extraction from the opening according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract it then as one piece of coarse cloth between your fingers at the front, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is scattered; make sure you do not stick in the opening, that you do not come up to all the inside skin till the eye, that you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision doesn't open at the beginning of the cut, increase the cut gently until it opens; then pull it as we have said, then moisten with cloths and water, and place on the wound, and strain with wrappings.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such places where they grind flax and place it to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment should be continued as long as he is sane.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there appears an abscess in the hand, then the treatment with plasters should continue as long as he is sane.
des poilz des papieres	"Des poils de papier" translates to "paper hairs". This phrase might be used metaphorically or in a technical context depending on the broader context of the text. Without additional context, this could refer to fine threads or fibers that resemble hairs from paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hair grows on the face in a manner not natural and as it ages, these hairs can cause trouble for the eyes and lead to various illnesses such as watering eyes, papillary swelling of the eye area, and albuminuria; all this is due to damage caused by the hair. And here is how one should treat: through a method involving fire (cautery), or with medicinal waters according to what was discussed in the chapter about cauterization methods, or it can be done through incision and suturing, or with threads, following what I will explain next.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary for you to place the head of the eye in its healthy position, then turn over the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it turns correctly, that's good; otherwise, if not, you should pierce one thread at each of the two ends. And do this either inside the margin where hair grows or right above these hairs on the paper. Then draw the second thread across all the paper, and turn them over with a rasp tool. Afterward cut through the part under the paper, under the adjusted hairs, until you reach the corner; then extract one thread, insert a small cotton tent and lace inside the paper, then mark an engraving on the paper like a bay leaf pattern. It is also necessary that the figure matches the size of the raised area of the paper as it's marked for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there's part of it that requires handling with great quantity according to how the paper becomes soft; then do so over the entire spatula on the two lines you have indicated, and start with the large oil jar until it gets smaller; and make a fissure near the natural hairs in the growth size of a root, then place an ounce at one of the two corners of the keel, then burn everything else; then join the two lips into a stitch with a fine thread on all one needle made of wool, and let blood out, and let dry the excess threads on both sides of the stitches if you see fit to do this; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches with dried and binding substances because the paper heals due to the adhesion of the wound and assembly of it, but the stitch gets moist (as was said by the old ones), and this work is without fear; and there's another way: you engrave the paper into a figure that is as like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, with three ounces removed according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	And cut that which crowns the lesser powers evenly according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the strength to hold the forceps, and the object is not even, then take a needle with thread, and insert it through the center of the object; and pull out another strand from a large hole, and the second strand from a small hole. Then lift your hand evenly, lifting all the skin above where you have incised, as we have described before, then suture the two sides of the wound together by suturing them. The cure should only be applied when it is clean. And if pus appears at your incision site, then apply ointment and soothing balm to it. And every time the paper hair turns out: you should use what we have said about incisions; but the suture in one or both areas becomes more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canes follows this form: and it is that you should convert the paper and make a cut according to what I have said, then create two canes by art, and two small stitches as well; they should be long enough compared to the paper width, taking into account the thickness of the membrane covering the eye. li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil. Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve. de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness, called 'congestion' or 'decay', comes to the eye, if it can occur in two ways: one naturally and the other unnaturally.

And the way to perform it is that you cut open this bond, and open the skin of the affected area, and insert linen wadding inside, and leave it until it heals; and you should not use in its treatment any things that dry up and restrict.

de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the fluid which comes in the eye

Accidents come from wounds, splits and cautery, and similar things. dou soudement de la papiere	right away from the paper

de la bowe de l’oil	By the way of the eye

de la char sor le neis	from the flesh of the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. And if there is nothing left that we can't take, then open it all up with two fine, light instruments, ensuring there's nothing remaining; and if you don't exceed your strength or encounter an abscess, treat it as required; and if they are malignant ulcers, hasten and cauterize them until the pus stops flowing and all the hairs are removed.
