Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have thick limbs that do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-crafted iron, and should have teeth for gripping during use.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during the operation, it is necessary to put moistened cotton with butter under it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the thighs are softened, then hold the pliers called "algefri," which make the cuts appear as if they were well cared for; and do it like a file, that is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you expose the entire flesh around the root, and put in the tool called "althali", which is known as pincers, this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it strong and large enough so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, use all tools, as their forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool which has two prongs, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other tools that are positioned before in the row of teeth, and with this tool that looks like a large pair of forceps, here is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And may these tools be such that they cannot be broken, and know that many instruments for teeth exist; and similarly with other tools which are not numbered; and let the wise master find his own instrument by himself, according to what his tasks and illnesses demonstrate to him. For there are parts of diseases where the old ones did not teach any tool because of the diversity among these, and if they break nothing from the caries or of other bones, or if it rots, then he seeks for the tools that suit him, which I have told you about, and aids in gestures, here is its form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well holding for keeping the bone, so it does not escape, but can keep and remove it; and then restore the site with medicines suitable to this, and if there is rot in the bone, and if it is small, then take all of this instrument to retrieve it.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and its shape is ugly, especially in maiden women, you should know if this tooth has been born after the real tooth, and it's not straight; then you can't file or grind it. Therefore remove it; and if it is mixed with the real tooth, take this instrument that is described here which has a form like half of a small beak, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file grinds slowly in your hands due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you don't move the others; and if it is visible that one can grind it, then use a single piece file as described here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And similarly to how one makes needles with the steel from nails; and by grinding down a tooth gently in short bursts, so that it does not move until it is thin; then in the end grind away completely without leaving any burr. And if the edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must smooth down the roughness of the edge until it is even, so as not to hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth becomes dull
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front is removed, whether through percussion or impact, and the patient cannot press it with what they eat so that it doesn't bleed, and you have treated them with restraining medicines, and this isn't enough; if you need to restrain it with gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. And the thread should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are fitting together, take the thread and the double end between two healthy teeth, then place the removed teeth between the diseased teeth, if there is one or more, until you can comfortably reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering up to the part where you inserted it, and pull your hand skillfully and carefully, so that it doesn't move at all; and tie your thread at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then hold the teeth with a thread using some forceps, and join them together, then place them between the healthy tooth and its socket. Place it so that it doesn't irritate the tongue; then leave it like this as tight as possible without causing pain. If they move or the thread breaks, use another thread to fix them in place. If it stays and serves well throughout its time, this is how teeth are supposed to look and fit between two healthy teeth, as you can see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is dislocated, if it's returned to its place, again and again, as we've said; and do not interfere with someone who isn't a professional or suffers from pain, and each time shape it like an osine (a type of bone) tooth, and put it in the position where the defect is, and hold it like we've said, and remains and serves thus for as long as needed.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of covering the wound on the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None of the ligaments that come from under the tongue or are natural to birth originate like this; or by accident in a wound that is stitched together. The procedures are as follows: you work on opening the mouth with the aid of the tongue, and hold your head above the healthy side, lifting the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament sufficiently wide until the tongue has moved from its place, and if there's stiffness or swelling, it's due to sudden trauma; if necessary, insert an uncinate into this area and cut off that particular ligament; remember not to let the cut be too high as there is an artery beneath; once you've completed your work, take away something of a pinkish hue or cool water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue for each night until the ligaments can no longer stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood flow is present, place the glass tube in its place; and if it fails to stop with this method, cauterize with the slow cautery iron, which suits such situations well; then proceed with other treatments until he stabilizes.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it being of any color or black or hard, such that the patient doesn't feel it, and doesn't touch it either, because it's a chancre; and if it has started to turn to blenchor, and there is moisture, if pus secretes, and one cuts with a fine needle, and discharges from both sides; and if it refuses you in your operation, then apply vitriol oil until it is completely cleaned out. Then return to your operation as long as you're removing all the force. Then raise the limb from the side and the heel, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No matter comes within the throat cavities which are called "godath", and they are properly referred to as two almond-like structures. When you treat them, as we mentioned in section division, and if they do not stabilize; be careful: if it's hard pus with a small sensation and fusiform color, don't touch them even lightly with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they're red and the root is large, don't touch them with iron for blood flow reasons; but leave it until it heals, then you will remove it, or it would break on its own. And if their color is whitish, and the root is slender, prepare your tool to cover, but first make sure the pus has settled and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient stand in front of the sun, and let him breathe evenly, and have his hands on his stomach, and have him open his mouth and hold his foreman's hand between his palms, pressing the tongue down to all the instrument, as it is shown; and may be made of silver or fine brass just like knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue to all this instrument and see the abscess, if one takes an ounce and puts it into the almond, and moves it above as much as you can; and removes nothing from the threads with it. Then control the tool, from which this is shaped, like some strength; and always make the head bent, and each to its place, and are very sharp, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument now, take the tool from which this is shaped:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be it sharp on both sides and named; and when you have done one almond cut, do the other in the same manner, and after incision gargle the patient with hot water, or water that is hot and easy to drink, and if bleeding occurs, gargle with hot water, or with cooked currant almonds, or bay leaf, or similar things, until the wound has healed; then treat them until they are well; and let no new abscesses form in the throat other than the two almonds, so cut them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which is known as the small abscess; and had nearly completely sealed off all of her throat passage, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked pathway, nor could she eat or drink, resulting in her death if she continued like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess was so high up that it had been placed two inches from the mouth.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I acted quickly then, and inserted an incision in one side, after which the other was cut out, with a large portion of the wound removed. Then made another incision on the opposite side near the nose, and opened it up to allow for mouth opening; afterwards put the incision back together again while pressing on the tongue; subsequently inserted the incision into the abscesses, and took away some part, from which only a little blood escaped; and thus cleared out the passage of the throat in this way, began now to drink water and then wine, not ceasing to cut parts of that abscess for a long time. And the abscesses grew back immediately, filling up the space that I had emptied out until they became quite large; then closed it up again and cauterized inside the throat: thus did not grow any more; and left those sections, only God made anything from him after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When return begins within the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is out of size large and round, it is called "eyeball".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment doesn't help, and you see that the extraction of pus has calmed down, and it feels soft, then it should be removed; and if it's roundly gathered together and isn't elongated; and if it's bloody or a blood-red color or black, then it should be avoided cutting into.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the method I have said, concerning its brightness and length, you should place the patient in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the tool we've depicted earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, move it around, and remove it after. Cut it using the two tools I mentioned for incising the two almond-shaped parts.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut too much, you hurt the voice and speech. And after incision, use what we have said about incising in the two amandros, and treat until she is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being cut, it is necessary that you apply something related to cautery for the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of the cautery is by using hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patient apply their head to your healthy part, and then press their tongue with the tool we mentioned or in the chapter on cautery, using a live sharp chaus, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the movement of this tool, as described here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hair or part where we apply the medicine, like how a spoon moves, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the wound; and the patient remains still on his side so that saliva and moisture flow from their mouth into the medicine within, not descending to the throat and the neck; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the wound for half an hour's quantity, until you see the skin dry out and the actions of the medicine cease; and when you notice this, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, soak the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument entirely covered with cotton above the cloth; continue to keep the cotton moistened over the wound as long as necessary; and do this repeatedly until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and heal after four days or five. And if you need to repeat the application of medicine cautery, do so, and after that, rub inside the wound with cotton dipped in butter, and clean out whatever remains within the medicine; and wash yourself with cold water, and continue gargling until fully recovered.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or the cautery method; if it's treated with fumigation following this manner, take calamus and rosemary, and oregano, and rue, and chamomile, and yarrow, and other similar herbs. Gather all of them into one pot or any of them alone in a single pot, place it in the pot, and bring to boil; ensure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot place one tool according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it of silver or lead, and let one of the shoulder blades lie in the mouth of the patient until the vapor goes up to the testis through the scrotum, while the testis is necrosed; after this repeat often, until the testis dries out. And remember not to perform this at the beginning of the appearance of a chaut abscess, for many things occur then; and do not do this as it declines in the chaut abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a thorn and place an eggshell in the patient's mouth, so that the throat of the patient does not become too hot; because the eggshell does not let steam accumulate on the mouth, and it makes a good treatment together for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it emerges in the throat bone or spinal column of fish, without anything else; therefore, if you must treat what you can see, press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument so that you can perceive any movement; and for what does not reveal itself to you, which is stuck in the throat, you should induce vomiting in the patient as if their food was cooked in the stomach; by chance if expel the obstruction through vomiting; or if the patient ingests a piece of sponge, a piece of navel, a lettuce root, or one small chunk of dry bread; and bind the sponge with one thread, then swallow it. And when it reaches its place, if it gets caught, and then pull forcefully; and if this does not work as what we have said, take one diving tool according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And have the instruments bent towards the head so that it may more lightly enter the throat, and raise the head high; and be cautious not to touch the epiglottis, that nothing might slip down or push the bone inside; and move when the patient pushes the instrument in, because if they are moving or obstruction is forced through; if it is pushed back down, or if it is pulled out forcefully with all the instrument evenly, until it is pulled out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never heal by the sweat of the patient, as I have said in division through medicine treatment; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient at noon, then press their tongue with the instrument I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see it bleeding, treat it with all possible precision, or use fine forceps that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a single hair and insert it into the throat of the patient, then push or twist the end of the hair until it becomes hot, and repeat this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you bathe the patient in water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then fill the eyes with cold water, and operate on the mouth, pour it in such that they cannot swallow, and move it often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will defecate.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it doesn't defecate as we have said, subfuse the patient with asafetida using the instrument mentioned for the eye treatment in fumigation; do this many times because it will expel without pain.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of fumigation is as follows: you take a pot where there are charcoal sticks and have it covered with a lid in the middle, and holes made through this cover for the tool's head to be placed. Then pour your fumigation, place the stick at the patient's mouth using the tip of the tool, seal their mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes up until it reaches the nostrils; now the nostril should start expelling (smoke), if not, repeat the fumigation several times and allow the patient to feel thirsty, consume salty things and similar items, don't drink water. Then it's necessary for her/him to exhale through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat blood is like this: when one can see it, it resembles curved scissors meant for entering the throat; and it has a likeness to a doctor's beak, and it is sharpened with grinding, so that whatever she takes, she cannot leave it. And here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter concerning abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Wounds from abscesses are, as the memory brings after one and another in this book, diverse both in puncturing and in size; and it is in two ways which consist of one that maintains its own appearance, and due to which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for when they are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses at the head are different from those in the foundation, and the abscesses within the body meat are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if one has abscesses that should not be pierced until the body is dead according to their completion; and if there are such that it must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses within joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, and it is left until they are rotten inside, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint have been corrupted by this, causing a contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For the abscess is within the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it's dead, it will harm the main limb. Or if it's within the foundation, then piercing or doing so when it's dead; and there should be no piercing of an abscess without digestion completed, except for that which is within the foundation, where it would rot from underneath, being inside, and lead to a fistula; and cannot heal properly over a large period.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of draining an abscess which is done according to completion, and this occurs when the pain subsides, and the departure of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and during the movement and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you keep the drainage hole as close as possible beneath the abscess, and where it opens outwards. And make the drainage hole long along the center line, and if the abscess is near the hands or feet, or at joints and in necks and arteries, and everywhere uniformly where there's no furrow.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses is in the fatty part of the body, it is advisable to wait until the perforation is confirmed after full completion of digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, then the body suffers from the poison of itself and is full of worms; and by chance hardens its skin and the inner parts of itself.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess pierced across the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you use small abscesses, small cuts; and for large abscesses, large cuts, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or it requires a seal, and covering; when they have become as stiff as cloth, and are softened, then it is necessary to do it like one does with wax: and for those that are split into three angles, and for those where you cover them like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses from angles; and for those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar cutting methods.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those without a head, like superficial abscesses, it is necessary to pierce them completely through. For large abscesses that have formed large blisters, if you prick all the blister in one go would not be ideal; instead, puncture only a part of the blister when first doing so; then let the abscess drain until reaching another spot, then leave nothing for healing; do this procedure multiple times with increasing size, until the whole blister discharges; similarly, if the patient has weak constitution, or is pregnant, or young children, or elderly and decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when an arrow pierces through, it vibrates several times with the exit of the bow, causing perhaps death to the patient, and you should not neglect this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be cautious in this chapter, and when you have made your incision if it causes a wound, observe whether the incision from the wound is small. If it's a simple cut, use strips of linen or old cotton; and for large abscesses with numerous pus pockets, place tents under each one so that they lie against each other. If you have cut into the pus sac through part of the skin and stitched it together internally, fill it with old cotton or linseed rags without moisture, bind it up to the third day, then apply dressing until it heals naturally.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood bleeding occurs in your operation, apply cold and gentle treatment, cover it with moist cloths, and place it in the correct position by doing so many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding continues persistently, apply a regulated treatment and care, using the powders I have mentioned in this book. If it's infected by ice or cold weather, and if your area or if there's pus present, it is necessary that you place wet cloths soaked in wine and oil on it; and if it's inflamed, and the area is fleshed out, then it's proper to apply wet cloths soaked with water and oil, or wine and cold oil until the third day, as we have said; and afterwards remove the pus and clean it, according to what is required, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in treatments of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of these
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For the small abscesses that come from the head, and are like our mannerisms found in cloths, such as a locket on a cat, and many resemble this.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are those that have too much moisture like grease and oil; and there are others that are hard and stony to the knifeman, and there is no doubt that they are arteries, not to do otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the knife are that you must try with all the tool called "intermediate", from which the form comes after, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then you cut through long over.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture has been drained, then scorch without leaving anything of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately if nothing is left behind; then dip cotton into Egyptian ointment if available; otherwise in water and salt, and apply to the wound, and let it heal until another day; and this will remove whatever remains from night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And begin repeating the cotton application, as previously described, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure it does not persist through the night; then treat the wound with an ointment suitable for that purpose, while it is still clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess remains hard, do as described in this form, longitudinally; and cut out your incisions, and peel it from all sides, and apply all your treatment force to the cloth where it is; and if the artery goes against you, then do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat the abscess if it is stony, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting on the stony abscess and wetness, it is lighter because there is little blood involved.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or head or there is no moisture, and from the foresaid abscesses that I treated or treated a head from an old woman; and found the abscess to be like a soft stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one had pierced none, one would have done as well to make incisions as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or towards the head, I have found that those which come near the child's head and the roots of their ears, the opening should stay open for as long as possible depending on the size, so that the pus can escape; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	regarding the instructions for dealing with scrophula (also known as King's Evil or leprosy).
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, under the armpits, and around the throat, and not anywhere else or on the body, they are small and interconnected.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scab is properly within its coat, like the nut and the abscess at the head, as we have said; and the appearance of these scabs are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that don't want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In this case that you see with good arrangement in the stomach, and it resembles the color of the flesh, and silent from each side and is not mixed with the muscles under the neck nor near the artery or in the ducts, and is not deep; then you should handle it above, and remove it part by part, and straighten the two lips of the mouth at the seams, if necessary as we have said about abscesses at the head; and cut a little bit at a time, and be sure that you don't cut the nerve or the vein, and that there is no spasm or trenching, so your hands do not escape and see too far ahead, making sure you only remove what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you sever the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to open it, then introduce vitriol paste into the wound, or any powders that expel blood, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed and the wound becomes soft, then begin to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound has healed, return to your work until you complete it. Then according to your skill, if there are any small pustules remaining, remove and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the pustule, it should not be severed directly from its root but rather wrapped with a thick doubled thread and allowed to fall out through that area without harm. Then dress the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then treat accordingly.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the whole scab, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and make the stitch now, then there's no need for excess due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you prepare to extract its root, and drain pus, and stitch as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scabs that are due to excess, pierce them wherever they have opened up and drain; then pierce in the same manner as previously mentioned, relying on it, then apply ointment and similar things, so that whatever is infected from decay rots; and when the wound has been properly cleaned, apply anointing oil over the flesh until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	Of squinching
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and discussed about the surgery of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squinching,[1] it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as "epiglottis" be made; and one should not attempt this, for all the veins and the lungs are vulnerable to illness in these who have abscesses either within their mouth or in the throat or .ij. amandines.[2]
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lungs, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Thus, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary to make the incision across three or four small cuts through, between two circles, or by the size of the cut, not in the cartilage; and this allows for the sectioning of the epiglottis so that there is no meat, and the vessels are long from within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they stretch the skin of the throat throughout the chestnut, then cut down to the keel until you reach the navel; and avoid any veins, if you see nothing, and then open the belly button, as we have said; and this can be demonstrated by the rupture of the stream in the navel which leaps out through the chest that has been broken, and by the absence of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed since one begins to doubt strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound as neatly as possible, and sew them all smoothly without the cartilage; then apply medicines that cause tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	All right, if you do not perform this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged as dead, and the defect remains.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut through the epiglottis because the organs cannot be moved, and he breathes from the wound, and thus you are saved from death; and for this reason, the elderly instructed to leave the wound open until the disease's malice has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and clean it, as long as it was cleaned; and I will tell you what I observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe. And I was called to treat her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found that blood was flowing from it, and indeed she did not have a cut vein or pathway leading out except for her throat, and the air entered through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurriedly treated the wound, and after it was healed, she was able to speak again; for this reason, I say that in tailoring the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat

dou chancre	And the ulcer.

Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So do not hurry to pierce it immediately, but let it die as long as the pain is relieved; and then have the patient sit on the stool, with two small stools under his knees where he leans forward, supporting him from behind and assembling his legs towards the parts in front of the leg; and make sure his buttocks are spread out, put his arms under his knees and bind them well with a good bandage; then encourage him to blow against his right side, and introduce an instrument into the opening of the throat, which follows next; it is necessary that when you see this instrument being introduced, you first determine the depth of the throat so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instruments are larger, cover the depth of the throat with cloths, so that the instruments do not weigh down on her; and have him put the funnel of the instrument above, and cut the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess has opened, and you treat it manually with gentle touch, one should cover it at its head, at its neck or in the pit of the shoulder blade; and when the wound is drained, it is fitting to put wet cloths in olive oil or in dried thistle oil; then place the cloth saturated by the wound's edge into a mixture of marjoram, and spread that on top with another clean wet cloth dipped in water or made with cooked willow leaves and aristolochia roots; afterwards apply this ointment after two days, until it heals; never lift off the marjoram and wound through a cistern of water and honey, then with water or with cooked root mixture of willows and aristolochia; then again, revive with this ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has returned to being in the marjoram herb bed, then you must guard against heating with iron, but treat it as we have instructed when dividing tasks.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Master comes first in the dance who knows the form of natural birth, and its signs are this: when you see a woman about to give birth from below, and smell the scent: then the child急于 to escape; you should understand that this delivery is according to the natural form, and comes out through her head, with the placenta afterwards; and when you see these signs, it is right to gently press her stomach, so that the child will come quickly; for when he descends from his head, it follows him, and is freed from his excesses by good delivery process; and this does not happen otherwise.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes at no time over its feet, and comes out through the body or shoulder, and hands, or comes out over his stomach, or belly, and is transformed by chance from his neck, and by other harmful shapes; this is necessary in the dance that she should be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the forms on how one must help it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the baby descends through its head by a natural outlet, and the woman experiences severe labor pains, if her strength is weak, she should sit on a stool or have women hold her. She should eat food from fenugreek that has been cooked, and then have the midwife place between her fingers a small spoon (spatumile), as shown:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut the second one, and remove up to his moisture until it is expelled; and take hold of the woman's abdomen as her child descends, and if she doesn't, then administer castor oil with fennel seed paste to the woman. Then have her drink and sneeze on consin (an old term possibly referring to a type of broth), and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now let the child come forth.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if her two hands come forth, you should gently pull them in and out; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up. Then remove the stool from under her, and cut open the woman so she doesn't defecate during removal; and if her hands can't enter and her child is dead, then use a knife that was placed beforehand, extract the child, and pull out equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on its feet, it should be lifted upwards; and then turn it little by little, until it is even; then press down on its feet and spread them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump to its knees, if you command and make it whine with consideration; if it jumps further, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't adhere as we have said, if you twist a little bit by a little bit, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore, make it lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it doesn't jump like we have done, say to take a muscilage of height and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; and apply this ointment inside and outside the woman's body, then make her sit in warm water until under her ribs; and when she is moistened there, make her wear myrrh collar, put it on her, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on the bench, then make her whine and restrict her mouth and nose, and lightly rub her stomach, because the child jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the birth takes this form, if she puts her hands gently and gently on him; then stand behind his neck, and hang his feet downwards from above, and let him lie on his side at bed. de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child which proceeds with one hand during

I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that you touch their hand gently, then turn it gradually and gradually, and lift them slightly. de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for all the second part.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for the whole second part, if you have removed the second part at your nail, as long as moisture is being cleared out; and if there's any child inside and under their chin and neck region, you should let her go from the birth canal so she doesn't get trapped, and kill the child; then expel the child inside, until you've placed them properly in accordance to how they need to be, and command that the woman pray every time: then gently remove her.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth canal
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born often, and sometimes three or four at once; this is not an unusual thing, and it doesn't happen frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are removed, and do not live anymore, if I am not mistaken; I know this much, that they multiply, and get burned by the fire which devises them, which is bound to the oven; and no more come out naturally like all under, as we have said.

de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They are never formed in the Maris I to XV or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like an infant by the measurement of the glorious womb, it is necessary that the midwife know all this because such a thing might happen to her; do according to what should be done.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another oak branch, or if necessary the third one, so that the extractions are equal; and then make them even by moving from side to side, for ease of exit, and ensure that the branches have teeth to hold during extraction, as illustrated here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, if there's a scab on some of its doves from that area, and treat it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if no part remains, then place this branch or higher up, and do as much until everything comes out fully.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back by squeezing, it's necessary that you wrap around the first glove until everything comes out; then cut in the place of the joint on the sole or at the wrist, and similarly do with the other hand, and for both feet.

And if the head of the child is large and it is twisted at the exit, or it has a sharp tip assembled, then you should push the spiny spur between your fingers, and form the head and remove the sharp; or you will cut it with the instrument called 'almidach', which comes with the tools or chapter after this one; and thus similarly cut off the child with large natural head; and then pull hard on the bones with tweezers, and if the head twists and holds to force, as long as the moisture at its base flows out; and if it cannot come out, you should puncture in pieces until you can move them; and if it is swollen in the belly or around the sides, then you must cut as much as the moisture runs.

And if it is twisted in the belly or at the udder, then you should pull it out by its skin envelope on the hand; and stretch the belly or the udder, until the moisture which is there runs off; and if any other member has osteitis, and the head remains, then push your thumb down from the palm of your hand, and pull until the mouth of the teat is reached; then push in a ring or two, and pull hard; and if the mouth of the teat has narrowed due to an abscess that came there, it would not be right to remove this forcefully, but it should be treated with moist and fatty things; and apply ointments, and dip into water-based soothing and moistening substances.

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom an offspring had died, then another one was conceived within it, and the other one was expelled by it.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for treatment, but I considered for much time, and could not secure the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed it on a strong plaster, and from it came out a bone, and after several days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed because this person's belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.

I attend to the wound, and with my hand in her stomach as long as the woman was at her best point; and I let the woman stay like this for such a time, and it so happens that she is slightly better by then; and I have remembered this chapter only because of what happens when masters find an unfamiliar thing, they should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the wife to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Next comes the form of the presser, with which one works in the books; and at two turns for each pair of four limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	In every way, the horns should be more delicate than a retractor, and made of ebony or boxwood. And let the opening at the end of the rod be about as wide as two fists, and the groove for the sticks should be cut, and measure half a palm long, or slightly longer; and in the middle between the two sticks there should be two attachments of the same rod, which must fit tightly in each other, from half a palm's length to somewhat more; and these two attachments are fastened at the mouth of the trough to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, resembling it more delicately and lightly, should be made of a rod from ebony or boxwood according to the appearance of the pincers; and have at its two ends two attachments, as you see, each about half a palm long, and two sticks wide; and when you observe the woman open with all the instrument, make her sit on the bed, her legs hanging down and her thighs spread apart, then position the two attached parts together in the trough, holding the head of the instrument between her buttocks; then work your hand over the entire instrument just as you would do with pincers in a similar way, according to how much you observe the mouth of the trough opening up, until it carries out what she desires.
