Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the bleeding is from a wound or its base, or an abscess, even when it's as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the thin clot where the skin is being compressed:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds in our division; now we will discuss hand surgery and medicine according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I state that wounds are varied according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and for why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The causes for injuries are due to the impact of stones, sword cuts and knife wounds, or spears, arrows, axes or similar things; they can also happen according to the parts of the body. For instance, injuries on the neck, head, chest, abdomen, liver, and other body parts. I will now describe how each injury is treated, starting with head injuries since my recollection will come in handy for this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs or bone is broken, and the bone isn't fractured, be careful if it's from stones or similar objects, and even though the skin has completely been torn open and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt whether pus will come out: if it starts to clear immediately from the head region in the same way as from the wound, and there is a little blood coming from the wound, then do a wet dressing on the affected part; and if the patient fills up with wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't start to clear, reduce their meat intake, and don't drink wine or eat heavy foods; put some on the wound, if pus comes out, use wet cotton in oil rosewater or rose water, or in astringent wine; and if no pus is coming out, apply to the wound, if it's fresh with all its blood, and isn't being dried by the air, with powder, which I will mention shortly; and if it has been dried by the air, apply some ointments until they are healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be stitched together with bandages, then stitch them together, as I will explain for wounds on the belly, by stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes the bone, it might stick but can only hold for a little bit if handled; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard tissue instead of skin, and instruct the patient to consume large meats like testes, cooked wheat, such as pulses, and similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or smell flesh decay, and it doesn't reach the bone, then extract all of the decayed flesh, pour out pus, then treat; and if there's an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, so remove the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this doesn't help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, treat them with a light cure: and you should put on this powder which seals in such a way that when the heat has passed, it stays firmly.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely grind them all into a powder. Apply this powder to the wound, packing it tightly until it fills well and binds with all the blood; then apply firm pressure and allow it to air properly without swelling. Don't remove the medicine until it heals completely, as you should leave it in place until it no longer swells.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one performs this only with salt alone, when one does not have the incense or the blood of dragon, but when the medicine has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the heart has healed the wound, even in that state, if you do not add this powder to it; but apply some digestible ointments, or oat flour made with water and honey, until it stops bleeding. Then treat further with other treatments until it is sound.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if bone bruising accompanies the wound and it's small, then apply fine forceps to it; and I will tell you about bone fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	From the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	That wound comes from the neck and it is simple; if there's no distinction between one and another in the neck or around the throat, but when the neck veins or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerves, without any other treatment than leaving the cure alone and not applying anything that restricts them, as they harm the nerves and make them recede; and don't place anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation with the spinal fluid is within the highest limbs; but use warm medicine, such as oil rinsed in soft water, mixed with rose oil, and other earthy substances prepared this way, and wet ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, one sews and binds it with bandages, then treats it as long as it heals properly.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and full of pus, if you pierce them or even below them; and if there's blood vessels cut, causing bleeding then, you must open it, seal it again, and cauterize which requires skill; and if the spinal cord is cut, or there are openings of blood elsewhere, guard any passage that food travels through, make sure not to touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then apply a dressing for days afterwards until healed. And if the wound has spread into bone, you must seek it out; and if pieces of bone exist, remove them all if possible, leave what cannot be removed till the wound heals and discharges cleanly before cleaning it and preparing the exit; and if the wound is fresh, apply powder as I've said on top of the powder.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has an opening, treat it as instructed in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Regarding the wound from a spear or a knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a lance or knife wound, and the injury is deep, observe if there's an airflow from the wound so you can tell that the patient might be in danger. If it isn't deeply injured, and it's fresh with all its blood, don't apply powder at first hour or bind it without the blood dispersing through the entire depth of the wound and returning to heart, causing stress on the patient; instead apply a healing ointment, bandage twice a day; and if you lack an ointment, fill the wound with old cotton to soak out moisture and let the patient rest for three days or four, or more; if no convulsions or heart tremors occur due to the stress of it all alone; once you see the good changes, and know that the injury is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it with other remedies and treatments as long as there is healing; and if it cannot heal naturally, work at it, knowing that there may be a fistula; treat it according to how one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it's simple or worse, or on the back, according to the treatment of whoever is present; if it's large, stitch it up; and if it's small, use powder; and if it's deeply in the bone, and pieces have been removed, then handle the wound accordingly, and let the removals heal over time; and for other wounds on other limbs follow similar judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	From the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Abdominal injuries are large, medium-sized and small; from a major wound there is often rupture of the intestines or their linings, through which foreign objects can enter. Stitching wounds in this area is more difficult and it's generally not better than smaller wounds, as when the intestines come back they're placed multiple times until it feels warm again because the intestines swell upon coldness; thus, a small wound proves better since one must massage the intestine back to its place compared with others. Know that abdominal surgery occurs in four ways: common stitches occur during abdominal surgery and other stitches for wounds on the body and other specific areas are common with other wounds; however, they're generally more precise when it comes to abdominal surgery, I will describe each of them separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I state that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestine sticks out, and there's no injury to a thing, this can be done by one of two methods: either due to the smallness of the wound as we have said or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it's cold, warm him in this manner: soak a sponge or dip a cloth in hot water only, or you cook it in boiling water with soap and herbs, and expose the intestine until the swelling is removed; and after doing this, make him sit up so he can release his swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, wet the intestine in water or heat and make sure it's cooked until it softens. This way, the entrance can take only a small amount of food; if it cannot enter that amount, then widen the wound slightly using the tool used for extracting worms; and after this initial treatment, allow him to eat as normal unless there is urgent need not to do so; this is the instrument to cut: if you carve inside along the curve and outside not, follow this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound has widened, and the intestines have been displaced, if you are able to reset it according to its natural form in its proper place, do so, because this is better than allowing it to remain misaligned.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it's in the abdominal area, you should make the patient lie on their back with their legs higher than their head. If it's below the belly, put the head and buttocks higher than the parts below; similarly, if there's an abdominal rupture in one of the two halves, position yourself so that the removed part is higher than the other; and thus you should apply what I'm saying about both large and smaller wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds use what you are equipped with, then have the surgical tools ready that cut the entire wound at your hand and stitch it together; and this is the common way of sewing. Use one or more needles depending on the size of the wound's width, and leave a space from the head of the wound to two inches, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce both ends of the skin with both ends of the suture needle that are inside the skin, until you have pierced through that part, then join the three parts together. Then tighten the thread of each needle inward around one side of the wound stitch, then join the two ends of the wound further on, leaving another space and insert another needle; then sew with this thread as you did with the first needle, doing it according to how many needles you need until all the wound is secured; use needles that are neither too fine nor too thick because the finer ones cut through all the flesh, and those that are too thick do not fit well: they should be of medium size; don't sew them too deep into the flesh and skin so they don't cut and damage the wound before stitching it together; then pull out the ends of the needles to avoid bruising the patient during sleep, and cover the needle holes with bandages or cloths for support until the wound heals; this type of sewing stitch is better for small wounds because a single second stitch is common, where you join both ends of the skin thread with both ends of the suture needle together at one needle that has strong medium thread. When you have pierced all four parts together, remove the needle from the part where you began in the way how you sew clothes and leave space between each stitch as large as two inches; this stitching heals the person, and I stitched a wound that had been cut open by a knife which was deep into the belly with a length of more than one palm's width, and contained intestines about two palms' width long, and it was in the center of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been there for 24 hours, and the wound healed up until 15 days later. I treated it and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when they saw that he was about to die, it was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointment since there was no oil or medicine where I was. Instead, I put old cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle, and insert it from the outer part up until it pierces inside; when she has pierced straight through from left to right, then hold the snout or side where you have inserted the needle, and make her pierce again from the inner part outward until she reaches the outer boundary. And with this stitching technique, just like a marten stitches fur, you sew in such a way that you leave one end of the snout on one side, then take it up on the other side, repeating until all the sewing is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, as Galen properly stated, is such that no one does this method naturally. They gather two parts together and apply the needle near each peak. Here's how it should be done: thread a needle or peak of silk near both peaks, then only pierce this area of the body, leaving the two peaks untouched; afterwards move the needle, have it pierce through from underneath until it reaches inside to the two peaks; then pierce through in both areas from underneath to inside as well using another two threads similar to silk that are on the other side; and this is how sewing should be done and is the most common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word and no one denies it: that one must stitch the belly with two needles or threads in each; and you should insert one needle from one side, and the other from another, like those who sew buttons. And know that when the wound is in the middle of the belly, then the stitches are more severe than most others' belly wounds.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are like those for other wounds: and when you find the fresh wound filled with blood, just as the surgeon has made it bleed, then suture back the intestine, and the skin; afterwards put on an attracting powder to the flesh. And if the surgeon has made it bleed, apply no ointment that might be available, until the wound heals; stitch up the incision, and the anus, and the navel; then treat the wound as for others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, as soon as it begins to heal properly, use old cotton wool, and clean it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in multiple conditions when wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound might affect principal members, it is necessary for you to moisten a light woolen cloth in oil of tempered heat or rose oil, and place it inside the armpits, and around the groins. And if there feels pain or gangrene in the belly, and happens repeatedly, then you should enemas black wine twice, and especially if gangrene comes near the intestines; and pierce from within, and know that when this is a large intestine, it heals more easily than smaller ones.

But if it extends so far that it enters through the bone completely, then it's called 'fistula'. And the skin is such that you can pinch all of the skin intact, also even when it is thin, like fine cloth; and doesn't open up from its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have noticed that the skin is burning and corruption hasn't reached all parts of it yet, and the skin beneath is full of pus, then treat with catharctic: observe if the breasts are large, and if there's a foul smell from them; thus prepare a cathartic with Egyptian medicine as follows: take ashes, oil, and litargy equally, put them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey; then use this according to your need, mix it with water and honey, apply it on the breasts, and hold the application down tightly; let the medicine sit for two hours, then squeeze out excess. Repeat this process until the breasts are freed of pus and dried up; if you do not have access to Egyptian medicine or ashes, use water from vine wood instead, pour some over the paste, let it soak in, apply, repeat until you're sure the breasts are thoroughly cleaned; if it is too harsh for the patient or doesn't tolerate the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then prepare a cathartic with water and honey, where honey has properties to clean and wash, while wine makes pus burn away. Once done, ensure that the breasts are indeed cleansed properly, then apply cathartic that produces pus in them, use plaster of Paris for this purpose; mix it with rose oil or wine. Alternatively, you can prepare a cathartic using other medicines and ointments whose properties I have explained concerning ointments; if the indrawn part is small beneath the breast, and there's no room for your catheter, widen slightly with an iron tool and apply a layer of Egyptian medicine or basilicon ointment until it is wide enough. If the wound is too large, make only a slit at the level where your catheter can fit in; if pus lies above it, pinch out the bowel or even further down than that.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowe is in place, one should not allow it to become contaminated; and if you are unable to cover over the opening as you see fit, do this: arrange such that the bowe goes down directly, without leaving any part of the bowe; take consolidating medicines to be placed under the skin, and they are laid out on the linen covering all the healthy area. Then cut close to where the hole is slightly wider than the first, so apply ointment on another piece according to the size of that hole, and place it under the hole towards health to alleviate the bowe, without removing much of the large linen until after several days once; whoever is under the hole in the chest, frequently remove for alleviation of the bowe, and know where it comes from the bowe, whether it's poison or pus or too much, or digested, or indigested; take care if the patient feels pain or no change, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner until you see the nature that leaps towards the hole of health, know that the chest is now healing, approaching health; then release in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound, change another linen, renewing the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts give off undigested excrement after many days, know that the breasts are not feeding properly.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if venoms are subtly cut after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are individuals who take too long to heal in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if indigestion comes across immediately after several days from within the breast, you should know that the breast does not recover. And if the breast takes a long time to breathe and is far away, adjust your medicines with dry and moist substances, as with ointment of diafinity, because there is a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take ointment of diafinity and mix it with roset oil, then pour it over old equal wine in substance; then cook and use it; and similarly, make cooked honey thickened when ointments of diafinity are not available, or you take myrrh and aloen and incense, grind them, and add the powder to honey that has been heated; and then stick this to a cloth and put it on the breast, and administer an aristologist longly, and lily roots which are also like powdered twice and centaury; and use simples or compounds: grind them, make into powder, place over the honey I have mentioned, and use it; and if the treatment lasts long without being cured by this cure, you should know that corruption has spread inward and made an impression in bone, or parts hardened, or limbs; if one treats the wound of fistula, as we said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the knuckle of the hand, or under the foot, or by chance in other toes; and when it becomes old, if one does not take care, then the abscess spreads, runs and causes damage for as long as it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it can reach all of it; and corrosion comes until the bone, as long as there is stinging pain, and the toes turn white and become discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have instructed in the section on division, and if the treatment doesn't improve the situation, then you should take action for it. Cut off all that remains of the nail, then apply a cautery to the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery should be quite large if the bone is healthy and the nail is intact. If the nail presses into the surrounding flesh, starts to poke out, and becomes inflamed, you should place the red hot metal under the nail so that it touches the flesh, then hold it at a height above. Cut off this thin and delicate part of the flesh gently, and apply heating and corrosive medicine onto the wound area in order to remove everything. Then treat with ointments until healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, you treat it by cutting and applying force, because as much of the bone that is corrupted, it can't heal. And if you see that the nail has become rotten, you cut it off immediately as explained before, then treat until it heals; and if it's hardened and splintered, and there's great pain when touched, you must first make it well. Then cut across diagonally above the nail bed while taking care not to cut too deep into the flesh under the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain from this. And if such happens, place something that soothes over it afterwards.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the numbness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	I must adjust those that are born in the hands of some people by chance and have thick flesh, and by chance there is part or they have bones, and none of them has a nail, and none of these are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in no way connected to the thumbs.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in any nook do not move, and those born at the joint sometimes do move; the size of the fleshy one is so light that it behaves like this: cut them down to their root using a broad knife.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which comes into being at the root of the joint is difficult to treat: hold onto the copper if you can.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one born or destined in any rear corner, it is necessary that you first cut down to the roundness until reaching the bone, then cut the bone with a thread suitable for this, and then treat him until he becomes healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The connections that come together at the joints are due to birth, or by the healing of wounds, or by welding with fire, or by similar actions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut this seam, so that it can be repaired according to its natural forms; then place between two moistened cloths or pieces of fat in rose oil, so they don't join together. Or you place between two delicate pieces of wood, until the fats are joined, just as it should be done.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When soldering, do it without using your palm, take care to perform the soldering properly as required.
des vils	of villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Vices are thick veins filled with melancholic excesses, which come from various parts of the body. More occurs in legs of those who walk on feet and work, compared to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So you should then administer to him one time the cleansing of colic, and then heal him of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron treatment follows two ways: one is by squeezing and draining the black blood, and the other way is to open the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure follows this manner: first heat the leg with boiling water for quite a long time until the large veins become thin. Then squeeze it from above the ankle to just before the knee. Next, cut open one, two or three veins, leaving them large enough, then drain out the black blood using your hand, continuously moving from one end to another until as much of this blood can stand the strength of the medicine; and then close up again and instruct him to eat meat that turns red in the presence of this black. And repeat the evacuation and cleaning whenever veins are full, thus benefiting the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment procedures are as follows: lift the leg from the sore area, if there's hair present, then put it in a hot bath. Then keep raising the leg in hot water until it turns red and inflamed; if you don't have a bathtub, heat it over fire instead. Position the leg on an artery for its entire length from the foot to the knee, or halfway up the leg between ankle and knee; then peel off the skin using vinegar, and burn the artery on each side, until you see blood come out when pressed - it should appear red and black, seeming like a white thread when it enters under the skin. Then burn over this point with fire, as if done before, and do this with another piece of skin; then peel off skin above the artery where visible, and hold up with a string, just as you did previously, and lift again with a small knife, holding for three times; then peel off the skin over the artery until it appears, and lift up with fire, following what was done before. Then burn with another size or sizes if needed, lifting them, pressing at heel to ankle, then moving back up to the second size; then squeeze from size to size, until it's all peeled out completely, then press again. If you can't peel and lift it, insert a strong double thread needle, hold and pull, then burn under this point, turning your hand from side to side till it comes out; make sure it doesn't burn too hot, as if too hot damage would come to the patient; when done thoroughly, place moist wool in wine and oil over the wound site, and keep treating until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the limb is twisted and turned together in a bundle, and it's not straight, as we have said, it should be that you cut it forcefully but do not twist it; and handle it as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron used to cut the bone is curved, and does not slice through but cuts instead, so as not to slice open a vein; and it has substantial curvature because if it were fine it would slice open the vessel, but being thick as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	from the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm areas where no plants or trees can grow, and on dry land with no moisture; and it may develop elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to putrefaction that comes from under the skin, just as serpents and worms cause it inside the body, between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of this vein's beginning occur in which there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then it changes one's limbs, and the vein begins to emerge outside, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And when the shoulder has been opened, it must be wrapped with a piece of leather about three and a half to four inches around the elbow joint, and then tied, leaving the leather hanging down on the leg. And every time there's any excess coming out, wrap it back under the leather and tie again; if it becomes too long, cut off some part of it while wrapping it again without cutting its root until it is completely done. Because if you cut it, it will get inside the flesh, cause pus and decay in the limb, leading to a bad sickness; for this reason, it should be treated little by little up to about five inches long or ten inches at most and another inch of the elbow's length after which it issues, and when you cut it, cut one rib or two and pierce until the bottom so that everything comes out. And evacuate all the substance inside, and apply medicines for decay on each day, then treat it like abscesses afterwards.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein with small cuts, and likewise when it opens in the ankle or knee joint, or indeed where the bone is, much damage comes about, and from such small wounds; thus treat then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that come out between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "the cow disease", because it often afflicts cows, and it's a small worm that comes out between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body going up and down. Its presence can be felt as pain moving from limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and then escapes; and it is accompanied by gangrene of some fluids, such as veins and worms and roundworms or in the stomach; doubt arises regarding its malignancy because when it travels through the body, and when it ascends to the head, and arrives at the eye, sometimes it returns and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and healed, one must only consider when it will end: thus, it is necessary that you tie the limb above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut upwards and start treating, and if the cut is made in proper alignment within the flesh, and you cannot find it, then burn it with fire until it heals; and the biggest nuisances caused by this are when they hurt the eye, as we have stated; and if you see it coming near to the eye, then restrain it from below using a piece of material shaped like a snail, then cut upwards, and start treating; and one should use the remedy of purification through the body's medicines in a dissolved state for the bad humors present, and beware of eating cooked meat that leads to putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from wind.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land 'vakirir', and it is a pain that occurs in any limbs, and then spreads from limb to limb; and I have seen this as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to attend a sick woman, and she revealed my arm to me, showing a small swelling in the vein of her arm. And soon after, I saw it ascend as if a worm were at her shoulder, much faster than anything else, just like hot silver when cut from one place to another; the pain withdrew from that spot and settled into her shoulder, then shortly afterwards spread throughout her entire body, until she reached the other arm; then she told me that it was now moving within her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved from member to member in such a way, for I had never seen this disease like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	In every case, I've wanted several times to move the pain from one part of her body to another, but I didn't do it as such, just as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was due to the woman's wet body, and having exposed veins, and due to that constrainted wind; and they don't seem to understand according to this reason with those who are delicious, and have wet bodies and reclusive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see the treatment for this illness, and the patients feel that pain, if it opens up as we have said, quickly seal above and around it, and then apply pressure until the wind's force escapes from the body; cauterize the body; and if you do not see it at your fingertips, treat those with wind disorders, such as stinking pills, pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearances and the locations of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them lies in the fact that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and soldered; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where pieces are found; and those that release in no member but release according to two ways: or within the main body part such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it dislocates then not at all in the position of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, presents itself: so that you must be prepared for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various arrangements; and when this bad sign does not present itself and the arrow is not fully extracted, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow dislocates and pierces the bone, and springs the fluid that is under the brain, it's when blindness and numbness and inversion and redness appear in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and confusion, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes loss of smell or from nose or ears; and sometimes loss of speech and voice; and a white moist discharge from the wound similar to pus, and also burns like a scorch; and when this sign presents itself, then take action and pull out the arrow if it isn't yet.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it is deep or in the heart shows that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck into something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow also ceases moving like a pulse, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore know without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never reveals itself is when there's no frothy discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with coldness.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow exits through the back of the thigh, it's below the small ribs; and there's intense bleeding and pain and sighing; and all limbs from the shoulders downwards move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach contents escape through the wound by chance, there is no matter of undigested meat in that.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach contents escape through the wound by chance, and there is nothing passing through the intestines in that jump, then there is no hope for treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow penetrates into the bladder and urine escapes by jump and leaves, causing great pain to the patient: know that this wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and shoulder blade and back spine and ribs and the legs, and seemingly similar limbs are safe according to various arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in your nerve or artery, and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you did something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one of the people when an arrow hit him under his arm in the root near the nose: I probed it and pulled it out from the other side through the fat of the ear, without much difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I pulled out an arrow that had hit him in the fat of one eye under the paper skin, and the arrow was stuck fast, so only its tip could be reached towards the shaft. The player was alright, and no bad incidents occurred to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And one arrow from the throat to a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow in his ear: I would have shaved him, and made incisions as I pulled the arrow, and he recovered the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled out an arrow from the house, that it was stuck in the chest or belly, and I thought he would die; and then when thirty days had passed, it did not change its position. I cut into the arrow, attached a tool to it, and pulled it out, without any bad accident occurring.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you find a house to which an arrow has fallen or struck, and it healed up on the spot; and the arrow remained inside, not changing its natural positions, nor did it find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And to another man, who was hit by an arrow in his face, and had the wound stitched closed; and ever since then has suffered great pain; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And one day an arrow struck in the face of the king, penetrating his nose and was leaning slightly to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called for treatment after three days following that incident.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to remove it with all my skill and did not feel it; and he felt pain and discomfort in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it might be from the tip of the arrow. I put a drawing plaster and digestive on his face because the ears were not swollen; and I saw the arrow in the ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days, and treated the wound right away, causing the patient's pain to last long periods, until they felt the arrow inside their nose; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive mercury medicine to the wound for days until it was opened, and tested it; felt the tip of the arrow reaching into his body. Then I adjusted it within the wound opening with that corrosive medicine until I could clearly see the arrow's head. I persisted in treating the wound terminally for four months, then healed the cut so well that my forceps fit properly, applying them from one side and the other; they couldn't be removed. Therefore, I continued to refine and invent various tools ways until I successfully used a pair of well-made forceps on the first day, according to what would be described at the end of this chapter when describing its form, treating it and keeping the wound open until healing took place.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they decide that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and the wound was sealed, and fully healed the patient completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I told you about the quality of extracting arrows, so place your treatment on what I do not mention, because books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters compare well on quite a few small things, and on that which is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the reduction of occurrences that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I state that arrows enter the body through two manners: either through their length where they penetrate, or from another side; and the one which jumps through or enters through there, it is an arrow going into the flesh, and now no longer shoots.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, let her grow until the skin is fully healed inside and she has recovered; similarly, if she's stuck in bone and cannot come out, leave her like that for a few days, and remove each day. And then she will jump, if she doesn't, drill through completely any subtle opening while the limbs are still wide, as long as the body's insides are fully expanded, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and reaches up to one of the brains, or if any of the incidents that I have mentioned occur to the patient: do not try to remove it immediately, but let her stay until she recovers after a few days, for when the arrow comes up to the sinus, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only buried in the bone and does not penetrate fully, and stays there for several days without any bad incident, if the device to extract it is used correctly.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's deeply embedded and can't come out, if you apply thorns internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is reinserted within the body so deeply that it cannot be seen, and one must feel its presence throughout; and if you can sense it when you try to remove it without any suitable tool; and if due to the size of the wound or the depth of the arrow, there are no bones, nerves or veins, then make it as large as possible; and try to pull out the arrow when you can, and if it has holes where it holds on, remove the flesh that is stuck in from both sides until you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, so you would pull it more harshly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't achieve this in one go, leave it until the arrow shaft is completely rotted, then remove it, as extraction requires agility.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if it goes against your blood flow, then apply what we have said about treatment in this chapter; and guard against cutting the nerve and vein, and perform the extraction smoothly without risk or abruptly or harshly or firmly or gently; place the patient according to their position before the arrow hit them. As it is the greatest aid possible for them. If you cannot do so, then leave them as shown by what the sign indicates.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that came from the other side, or if there appears anything unusual on it, or if the skin is swollen in some spot which you might see or feel differently: cut up there, as long as your forceps can take hold, and then pull: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, let it be still for now, and then resume extraction until the arrow comes out; and if there's an end of the arrow where it is, force that completely. And if it’s just a bit of flesh, and you see proper administration being given, if I provide the tool with a curved edge, so that the point of the arrow enters into the groove of the instrument; and then force it, and if the arrow is inside the instrument, force the tool at its pointed end, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is covered, it is necessary that you cover all the flesh inward or where I come in, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is in the chest or liver or bladder or ribs and it's close to important organs, you should cover above, if possible; but avoid covering the vein or nerves. Then remove what needs to be removed, then suture the wound when necessary; and treat until she heals completely.
