des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common bodies
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins from which bleeding occurs are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen heads: Two tubercles located behind the ears, known as "herb", and two arteries in the two visible temples; and two veins that are within the corners of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that runs through the forehead; and the vein that is at the nose root; and two jugulars which are found on the neck; and two veins above the mouth's lips, these are known as "augerich"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly treated consist of each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it's on the left side of the body, and people call it the "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called 'fascia', and it's made up of the cephalic and basilic veins, and people call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein either lies on the left or right side of the body, and people refer to it as the "vein of the belly", and is located under the collarbone, and that's the one we treat, which opens clearly underneath the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The veins which are found between the little finger and the ring finger each have two, and in the leg there are three veins: one is near the bend of the wrist on the left side of the body, and the second is superficial and located at the ankle on the right side of the body; and the vein that is called 'the knee', which is found at the ankle on the other side of the body. In the other leg there are three veins under these.

des sainies de ventouse	Extraction with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or spiders, or leeches; and bloodletting can be done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction technique which can cause pain is done in two ways: either with fire or without; and the suction that is performed by causing injury and bleeding extraction takes place through fourteen parts of the body, from which one part is completely covered at the head; and another extends around the neck; and two others are located on each side of the neck; and one suction cup below the chin; and the suction cups of the two shoulders; and suction cups on the arms; and suction cups on the legs; and suction cups on the calves; and this suction procedure does not remove blood because there are many small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and due to that it weakens none at all, as with bleeding treatments; and it should never be administered either with or without fire in any illness caused by overeating, until all parts of the body have been emptied.

Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup to be used on fire is as follows:

And has two fingers of about half a palm wide each, and at its center near the midpoint one small notch, just like for driving a nail in, whether with an iron or brass tool, such that it does not cause injury when placed on the body; and at the middle place across from iron or steel bar to hold an oil lamp, and they are large or small according to the diseases and age of those taking them; because the suckers of children differ from adults', and for瘦people than for fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one should place this suction cup on the body: take the wick or cord of beeswax, and insert it through the bar in the suction cup, ensuring light is at the bottom of the suction cup to avoid burning the patient; then put it on the body, and your fingers at the notch that we described, so when one desires, if steam goes out, remove the suction cup; and take the wick or cord as before, and repeat often, should you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in the disease of pleursin, there should be neither excess nor deficiency, and it is only used forcefully when it is full of water, and placed only on the limb; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without applying suction only to limbs where it's not possible due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar body parts; and on the naked areas of flesh, like elbows or knees, and other similar areas. The quality of application is that when you find withoutews in mild water free from dirt, you take them; and place one in mild water until they are comfortable and have nothing inside their stomachs; then cleanse with a bloodletting and suction cup treatment, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place on the withoutews. And once they're full, and start to pull away, if there's a part where you can apply suction, then apply it, because this works well afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the arm out of water, then cold water quite well, and then rub it. And if it heals too quickly after the removal of the stitches, moisten with linen cloth in cold water and place over it until the skin is dry; and if there are multiple wounds, put on powdered vitriol or gall or similar things until they dry; or you put half a peeled bean under the arm, leave them to dry out under the arm, and will stop bleeding now; and if you need more, take other stitches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not heal well, rub the fresh bloodied arm or stick an awl in them so that blood comes out, then place it over it; and soon as they smell the blood, they will dry. And when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle a little myrrh and ground saffron or ash on it, they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and in the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear boy, that in this chapter, the foolish people throw away knowledge they don't see in any old books or read letters about; and because of this reason, the science has been separated from our land. I have never found anyone to be good at it; and I know nothing myself; as I learned through the sciences in old books that I studied thoroughly until I dealt with the science, and through experimentation, and by getting accustomed to my life's routine. And I am describing what is contained here in this chapter to you, summarizing it briefly at the end, clearly showing the forms of tools used during treatment as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to outline the contents of this book in our preface and specify the chapters where wisdom places its understanding, and remain faithful to truth. So that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when any fracture or dislocation or twists or swellings occur in any part of the body, it is necessary for you to quickly cleanse the patient from both sides with a hot application. If there's nothing too difficult about this task, like weak constitution or young children or old people; if the treatment area isn't very dry, or too cold; and avoid consuming cold foods such as cold jugs, and liver and fowl meat, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and don't fill up with meat that fills veins with blood until you are unsure of pus formation in an abscess, or spreading of contents to the limb. If the patient's condition improves according to their usual routine after this initial treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that are rich in nutrients, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and peas, and pies, and veal liver, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And with this kind of nourishment, healing occurs more quickly and the break heals better.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that when bones of the old and the decrepit cannot be mended or sutured according to their nature due to dryness in limbs, or also those that are too tender such as children's bones; but instead, reset upon the broken bone with the big joints and connect the limb together until it resists as before; and do not end his work suddenly, for this requires nourishing of large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all about fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures going to an arrow wound, and others while sharpening, such as when cutting the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a fracture with injury, and a break due to a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its own tool and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory brings to his mind; and it is known that bone breakage is recognized when the limb is twisted, opens well through the exterior, and presses under the hand; and when there is no twisting or swelling, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no breakage; but it can well have twisting, or a crack, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But it is not appropriate for you to move it with your hand, but apply the following remedies and then gradually constrain it now in a subtle way.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that when the breaking occurs within the body, and it is divided into two parts at the joint, you should now place them at equal points in alignment as though they were an abscess or vein opening. And if the abscesses are left open, you should not allow any delay until the abscesses have healed; then align them so that you can gently and wisely move them. You should know that restoring the body after a break is easier than after injuries with pieces intact. Then restrain it as detailed later on.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces broken in the bone, and it is divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or one of your smaller limbs, or at two cords, or at one cord and with your hand; place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member have healed, you gently move all attachments within their limits as best you can, and make sure that through your work no harm or pain befalls the patient; and adjust both ends of the bone joints according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it's not quite right: if the positioning is beautiful, and don't strain it too much, don't press as those who extract by their art do for pus discharge and muscle tension, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, chastise well the patient so they do not move it, neither awake nor asleep, neither turning over, nor in any other way; and see that the limb is securely placed so that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they do not feel any pain, it is not in its proper place, and you should put them in a suitable position so that no pain is felt; and guard to have been placed straightly, such that no twistiness occurs upon restoring them. And the quality of the broken limb will be according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied in size and extent, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are smaller limbs, such as hands and feet and alike: it is required to envelop them with soft and fine linen cloths; and for those that are larger, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a broad and firm band, because the wide bands embrace the entire large limb and constrain it uniformly from all sides, so there is no twistiness. Then tie around loosely, three or four times according to the limb, and restrain your hand somewhat throughout the band, then go beyond the breakage point and restrict less, allowing the breakage point to move slightly; and soften the band little by little until you cover a large portion of healthy flesh, then take up another band, turn around tightly on the broken part. Then return to the region below the breakage point and slightly restrain it, not too hard nor too soft, as we have said above in the first lesson; then place linen or cloth bands between the tied linings, until they are all uniform, then tie everything over the bandage, and then put your well-made stars on top, if there is pus or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then put something soothing to the abscess over it and remove the swelling, allowing this for a few days; after that tighten them, they should be half the width of a hand stretched properly, or of the shaft made from pipes, or from palm leaves, and adjust according to this form:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the needles placed over the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; they should also be as long as needed for the size of the limb or its magnitude. Then tighten them on these needles in the same way you did at the first application, then wrap another lengthwise thread above them as was done before with the splinting; now make it tighter here, and less so there; and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be made of soft linen. For if the threads are too large, like what artisans who make their linen threads for string use in bandaging wounds with them, this is a big mistake because the application cannot be even if it is too fine, and there must not be less than half a finger's width between each needle.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the muscles are injured by the pressure of the shoulder pins after constriction in their healthy areas, then place them with linen or coarse woolen patches, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is under strain and the ribs are broken, I will say the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to forcibly stretch all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not suitable to use these plasters for more than seven days or nine, according to your condition of pus coming out from any abscess; and here is the method of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that stands on mill walls, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick, then use it. This is the common method of plastering for restoring fractures in various positions, equally so for men and children as well because it isn't excessively cold or hot.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations: take 3 egg whites, ladani, anise, asafetida, and gum arabic, each in quantity of .x. Z; myrrh and aloes, also each in quantity of .v. Z; garlic Z viij.; make this into a powder, then mix it with plenty of eggs; if the composition is hot, use this plaster because it has good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for using plasters to treat torsions: take mugwort and valerian root, add ten parts of each; add nine parts each of myrrh and aloes; add six parts of opium; and ten parts of Armenian balm. Grind them well together and mix with water or plenty of egg. Administer it as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method to treat injuries and fractures of joints and bones in their original position, and alleviate the pain caused, and when sawing uses bone, and bruising: take new wool, and the fat cooked in oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Wound plasters do not heal completely, but they are better for soothing abscesses and properly treating bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for dressing broken bones that heals them: take dried fig leaves and earth-pine leaves, grind them together, and make a dressing.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for plastering in the restoration of bone fracture and for alleviating the removal of pus.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of vismalve, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of cloves, from each one part; and grind it, mix with wine, and if the limbs are heated, mix with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method for setting more strongly than the first, when an abscess is starting to heal at the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and sesame seed, balsa wood, marjoram, garlic, and violet flowers and chamomile blossoms, take parts of all; grind and mix with salt water, or sweetened water, or with wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ippocrates states that one should apply on the broken member for restoration only a salve made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and asserts that it should be neither too soft nor too hard between two.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen suggests that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, things that are dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take mugwort and ome feathers or bird feathers, and sage, and equal parts of them, grind them together, make a plaster from it, and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then after a little while, take care that the patient does not feel any pain or strain on their bone in its place; do not remove it manually and if there's pain at the site, or itching without rest or swelling, if you notice this, quickly remove it and replace the setting paste. Then use a light bandage and wet sponge, soak them in water, then immerse your limb until the itch subsides and the pain is relieved; then leave your member to rest for an hour, after that place it on a dry skin, moistened with water or oil of roses, bound with a cloth, until you are sure there's no infection; and relieve inflammation at the limb site, and remove any discomfort, then continue the gentle application, and a bit more setting paste, but do not strain so forcefully as before; apply the paste carefully until it is set.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus is discharging and turning red with pain and swelling, indicating an infection throughout, then you need to apply plaster and bandaging, so reapply it in the same manner as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if no part comes from what we have said, or if the dislocation is only released after three days or four or five or seven; and do not leave it for twenty days according to this method, until the healing process finishes, and gets closer to putting back the flesh; then you should keep the restraint more than the first time, allowing its growth of muscle substance as I mentioned earlier; and if you see that the limb dries out more than necessary, know that injuries will not come; wash it with hot water each time you release it, and do this once every three days, clean a little bit at the wound; through this process cut off any injuries on the limb, and hasten the work of those who are ignorant and return the limb wrongly: this is harmful, and such works are foolish, and I see no other than to leave it and operate it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	regarding various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes occur. The causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and necks break entire bones up to syfac which is below the bone, such as when struck with a halberd or staff; because this manner of fracture is called "halfage" due to this method of breaking.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword penetrates through the bone from above without piercing it, this type of fracture is called "complete" fracture; and both large and small wounds result from these two types of fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact or a crack or a fracture in the stone, or through a stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture present, which comes close to the ligament that surrounds the bone, or above the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is healed within the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack small, this manner of fracture is called "hairline" because of it. And if the injury is caused by hitting with stone or falling or by some other means, causing part of the bone to be pushed inwards, making the pieces separated like blacksmiths do when heating inside their furnaces; should the stone penetrate inside the body.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have wet bones, such as in the neck of young children; and occurs in all these ways when small fragments are lost, like in a case of splintering; and I shall explain about it properly.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all ways of breakages by their diminution upon them, and the investigation in tests, and by the corroded flesh which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known through this: when one has revealed the bone and rubs it all around, if there is an opening of black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a breakage, beware of the illnesses associated with hair loss, and if you do not encounter any harmful incidents such as vomiting bile, mental confusion, extension, pallor, fever, and other symptoms appearing in various conditions, there should be no doubt about recovery.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming incident, yet still hope for recovery, begin your treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the first snow comes to you, and it's winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the snow starts.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's winter, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that pus forms under the bone and the incidents we've mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the breakage of bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the broken part like this and take hold of the bony fragment from the body's side and expose it on the bone in all possible ways as far as you can, and more than that according to the shape of the wound. If blood draining occurs while uncovering the bone or if pus emerges, use what is necessary, then fill the cavity with wet cloth soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the pus drains off and there's no sign of bleeding; then begin working on the bone from inside, this process can be done in two ways: one way consists in cutting precisely forward at the edge and that's the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then use another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different sizes of cuts, some narrow and others wide, they should be pointed, and made of metal; and apply them lightly to the work so as not to pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it should be pierced through (from both sides), so that cuts are made with needles, not completely through until they pierce beyond the bone at the tip, and there should be a margin or a circle above the point, which doesn't let the tip pass beyond the bone; and you need more than one, so that each goes to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have needles for all sides; and this is the shape of the three methods of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the broken bone is that you place one needle on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then put the needle in another spot a bit after, and do this throughout, then carve out the distance of the bone which is between the breaks using incisors, as finely as you can, and gently, just like we said, so long as you are able to remove the bone with your hand or any tool you have such as forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is fitting that you reset the preparation which remains from the bone to every other instrument similar to an incisor. But it must be firmer and more delicate than the other incisor; and if there is no part of small bones or any scales, gently rub with them on the tools; then cure the wound with bandages and treatments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this which Galien stated, which is safer; and the force is very much, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone where the break opens outwards, so that once you have uncovered that part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision tool, which is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, and let the cut extend to both sides of the part, so that the cut faces towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer gently over the whole bone, taking care about the cloth below it. If it is tight against the bone, gently rub against the bone, for you will feel no harm or fear, as long as done properly and carefully.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks without piercing through the cloth, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces left, then after that abrasion, use the subtle scraper to remove scales. You should have various quantities of this tool so you can provide the most suitable treatment for each area according to the workpiece and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you stand before many rough judges, and then even more subtle ones, and never stop doing this until it's done properly.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other's haircut trimming and subtle breaking, it is necessary that you adjust according to their orientation; this thing cannot be answered by the one who has devoted his studies to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the shoulder dislocation is discovered, you should take a linen bandage according to the size of the wound and soak it in rosy oil, then place it on the wound. Then take another double bandage, perhaps two or three layers thick, soaked in wine and rosy oil, and place this on top of the first bandage; do this more gently than you can, so as not to burden the dislocation, then administer a bandage over that without pulling too tightly; only until it touches the wound. Leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess subsides, then release the dislocation and apply healing medicines such as rosemary roots, bran of wheat, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things. Make a powder from these things, place it on the wound, then administer normal medicaments without causing irritation; be careful that the wound is clean at all times, do not leave any ointment or allow swelling to occur, for when swelling assembles on the brain tissue, it spreads and causes great harm to the patient; because if you apply something pungent onto the dislocation, it irritates from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take care, should any unfortunate events happen to the patient as we have described, if it remains uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fear does not come out only because of the medicine we have applied there, should it have this effect, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of roset oil and one tablespoon of glue, and put them on your forehead; then cure in the manner that is fitting until they are healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts below the nose are ever broken or only one by itself, because these are two bones; and this lower part is cartilaginous, it does not break, nor should you twist or bend it, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts breaks, you should pinch your little finger or pinch beneath your nose, and place that break evenly inside your index finger, and through your hand outwardly until the nose revives according to its natural shape; do this gently and be careful not for the patient to feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and cannot reach to the nostrils, you should place it level with the tip of a small stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is two parts, redo this method, and strive to restore it on the first day if possible; if not, after seven or eight days when the abscesses are subdued, then pinch under your nose with linen cloth strips where the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you apply heat from another source on the other side, if breaking occurs; and make the attempts so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer dictates to moisten the bandages with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I don't think it's quite right, but the bandages should be moistened with a mixture of egg yolk and powder from grinding stones. Then leave the bandage until the bone is hard and the cartilage tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And whenever you use goose feathers in lieu of attempts, and if you have one egg broth all around, and the wound stays intact, and blows on the patient from within; do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose as you're working on them, then put in a wad of moistened cotton or balsam-soaked cloth, or a pinch of wormwood oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you need to drain pus, place a poultice on the surface, made of saffron flour and powdered frankincense, mixed with egg yolk. de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured inside and there's no wound on the surface, and only the breakage is outwardly present, not broken into two pieces just inside, but rather like a fracture within, one can easily detect it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you bend your index finger into the mouth towards the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, then bend your right hand's index finger instead, apply gentle pressure to the fracture internally, and move it with the other hand outwardly, ensuring equal force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is dislocation of the jaw bones in two places, it's necessary to provide an extension of both parts until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or a rupture, then stretch them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk. Then place on the broken mandible wadding, and put on one piece of double cloth; and put on this cloth a large wedge well made, or a piece of leather equal in size, long and wide according to the mandible, and fasten it there as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest. And have them eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then readjust what has changed; apply plaster, mix it with powder from the mill along with plenty of egg or almond flour after you have removed the wadding; spread a light woolen fabric over this plaster. If the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change, leave them as they are until they recover; many times recovery occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if it comes to incisions or wounds that require dressing, you should carry out what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a breakage and wound together, reward none of the bone piece in has been removed; so delicacy is needed for using tools suitable to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains none, if the wound is large, place one dressing suitable for this on it to encourage growth until it heals.
de la forcele	by force of necessity
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strength is broken many times in front of the shoulder joint, and breaking occurs in three ways:
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedures are as follows when there is a breakage that occurs with injury: you need two assistants, so one can mark where the shoulder joint has broken and feels the broken strength; while the other extends their neck towards the affected area. Then place the breakage evenly on your hands, so it forms correctly and lacks any appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round piece of cloth or wool under the shoulder towards the leg; make its size according to your needs. Stretch and lift up the strength, hold the ball in your hand so that you can evenly place the breakage as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force by force outside, because it comes forward, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back with their shoulder, and place a half-sized pillow under the shoulder. Then have someone support the shoulder downwards until the bone of the force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the crushing to your thumbs, and if you find any debris inside, it is necessary to cut through; and gently pull the pieces apart. If the bone cannot join under any pressure, cut at one of the incisors that you have made. But when using this tool on the force, place it near so as not to miss it:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And appears like a spoon, and is not found inside, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the operation; and has two heads, as you see, and is one broad, and the other narrow, as is the incision in the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain about extracting debris carefully, if closing the wound, and if the incision is small, or you doubt about extracting debris carefully, if covering the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And when pus comes out, if there is moisture, spread oil of roses, and alcohol, and wine, and place them on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The grinding of the bone when it is in wounds and cutting size, involves placing the plaster powder from the mill on the bone and some yolk of egg on top. And she is fully restored after XXVIII days at most, and sooner for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	On the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder is broken or large within it, and not in its middle; if one hits only the shoulder itself. Handle according to the pattern of breaking, and reset following its natural form, using any method possible you can employ. Then apply a powder from a mill with plenty of eggs on top. Lightly press, and put a double layer of cloth above it. Then place a broad but subtle support, slightly wider than the shoulder; ensure this support does not touch any part of the shoulder when placed. Apply linen wadding where the support is touching, so the support fits evenly without gaps. After which you should tightly bind the whole thing into one large firm loop, ensuring that neither movement nor shifting occurs on its own from the shoulder's position. Watch each link daily; and whenever it heals slightly, you should rebind, keeping the support in balance if it has moved back to its original spot. And place the patient on their side with the injury. The broken shoulder will heal fully within 20 days or 25. When these numbers are achieved, remove the support, you should be sure; this is not bone that heals quickly.
