de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones which are called the pair of 'fosciles', from which one is small, it is the bone that supports the pit; and the other is large, and it is the bone located underneath, towards the little elbow; suppose only the larger foscile breaks or perhaps the smaller one, and suppose they come together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fractures are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is poorly done, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, if it's appropriate to gently stretch and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large bone that is broken, if it's appropriate to pull more strongly; and extend on his buttocks, elevate the palm of the hand higher than the others, and place the smaller fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross her bones against herself, with her buttock in front higher so she doesn't suffer any strain; then extend your assistants' arms to the side near their hand, or at their elbow, and another assistant at the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirrors evenly, according to their best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break into pieces, you place each in its location; and if there's none that sticks to one of them when you grab it by the heel, then you can't restore it to its place. So do surgery on it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if in the case of injury that leads to a wound, I've mentioned this specifically in another chapter; take the treatment for it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if during the beginning of restoration abscesses occur, then apply a bandage made from rose oil and white beeswax, such that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and place the bandage gently, so that once the abscesses have subsided.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then place the wax, and apply the plaster made from powder mixed with plenty of egg whites, until you insert the splints. Make sure that the splint (bone dressing) is somewhat more pronounced in areas where it hurts the most, being slightly wider than others; know that there should be six or seven splints arranged differently: either in one bone, or two; supporting more on the painful area compared to other places, as explained at the start of this chapter. And ensure the bandages covering the pain are soft and moist, neither too hard nor abrasive. Use threads made of linen for tying them, not too thick or too thin, as previously mentioned.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the member after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad events come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary for you to dip the limb in hot water until that itch subsides; and let the limb not be left to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the traction, and if the ligaments have been severed and the bones exposed, do it as seems appropriate.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if one takes care that no injuries can occur to the limb because it is too constrained, it's necessary to soften it with a poultice, and leave thus for some days, until the pains subside, and then retighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, or up to 20 days after releasing them.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Otherwise, or around this time, then place your hands on his neck, and make sure the neck is even, and be careful of movement and stretching, and sleep on his back; and know that this healing occurs in 30 days or 35 days, and sometimes in 20 days, depending on the compositions and temperaments of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and in its knuckles there are few injuries, and they only bend many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to keep their fingers together and straight in front of them equally; then place their hand on an extended surface, and extend the fingers of the broken bone, placing them evenly side by side until they are well aligned. And put a plaster and bandages, if no abscess forms, then place an elastic band according to the size of the hand; and wrap it in one linen fold.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is in the inner part near the belly of the hand's sole, make a ring out of linen and tell the patient to place it on their broken heel; and then stretch it with a long piece of linen, and have the band wrap around as well as can be, just like how big the hand's sole is, and stretch it, according to what fits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the breakage is at the front, it is necessary that you place one support above and another below on the heel, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie everything together throughout the hand, and seal the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the breakage occurs on any of the fingers, it's essential that you treat them equally, just as is proper; and restrain with the heel, and should you see if placing a small upright support helps to lift the breakage, and doesn't move; and if the breakage is in another finger, like in the index or one of the others, do the same, and tie it using the healthy one that follows; or tie them all together with a single band, until you can properly treat it, or place a support similarly, as we hold them. Pay attention to the restoration and arrangement of each wound separately, and take care of those who come before you, just as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken foot
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see this when it turns in front and behind; and its restoration thus consists: i. the joining above the breakage, and ii. another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And in the patient's abdomen, then extend each minister his link to its equal part; and this is when the break has entered into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the breaking occurs close to the root of the heel, then it should be one of the ligaments towards the knife and the other ligaments under the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the knee, then you should have the ligaments within the knee, and the posterior extension; then place the sights on the flat bone at both of his hands until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply plaster and the bandage. If any pus comes out, let it go.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess to be treated with cautery, let it heal before you return to your work and treatment; the incision is made in such manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the break with a bandage made of two or three layers, and retain any excess. Then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the thigh, and insert the thread longitudinally between the heel and the leg, under the knee, and attach the head of the thread to the top; then proceed wrapping on the leg and the heel, then place a plaster over the break, and a piece of bone from the leg; then fill in between the leg and the heel with strips of gauze so as to evenly apply pressure. Then start tying forming three or four turns around the break; and when you go further above the break, tie less tightly; then check two ends of the thread that you have inserted between the leg and the heel, and tie them into three plaques placed at the top, then return under the head of the thread until you reach below the foot; and apply pressure to prevent it from moving in its place. Then leave him like this, and if no pus, swelling or similar symptoms appear.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, loosen the binding and address what has occurred, just as we have said many times. And if there are pieces of bone that are being gripped, if it is possible to cut them off, do so; and if you can't, it's appropriate to cut through the cloth and drain out force (hemorrhage); and treat it in the way we've described, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And not once is the flesh broken like when we insert needles, such as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, no complaint comes from the patient during this kind of restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the flesh is restored in one week, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that within the knee joint there is some cracking noise, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it's just a crack, or it loses connection and occurs in every wound, and feels like a wound, and this is felt very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: you should put in equal what was removed from its place until it can move freely again when assembled. Then apply plaster and add a round splint if necessary, then adjust as needed. Proceed with all the preparations we have described for other fractures, such as abscesses or similar occurrences. For each situation, apply what suits that particular case while maintaining soundness.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is named "mustelz" by the right and the other is called "foscile"; and any injury or fracture occurs just like it does with an arm. And this restoration procedure is similar to that for the arm, and all operations are the same. And if both of these bones break together, then the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn towards the front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and can see it clearly; and then it turns around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	So apply the procedure of extension and make it even, then evenly connect the nodes; but still, if the fracture is ugly or there are multiple fragments, that the extension should be lesser and more gentle. And adjust it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two furs of horse hair that strengthen the leg on both sides, and they should be as long as the length of the leg from the knee to here. Then wrap them in two strips each over and under it, and tie them in the middle, so the leg cannot bend either right or left, and thus it is well; and no one administers a bandage that is as long as the leg, made of fur, and they place the leg to ward off movement, and this must be done precisely where there was injury; and move the leg every day to see if there are any signs of an abscess or other accident; treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones due to injury
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	Ankle injuries do not come from breaking, but in bones due to injury there is a break sometimes and the bones themselves, only distress occurs in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there occurs a break in the bones due to injury, and you see these bones mount over one another, place such wounds on the ground like they would want to go, also as it were. Then put your foot on his foot at that point where the bones are raised, press them so much that their life returns; then put the plastering materials in the middle, cover them up, and place a small table under the belly of the foot with two shoulder-width planks, then bind them to the foot's inner side. Finally, wrap cloths around them or other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if you release the bandage, because you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the ribs are broken, mend them, as we have said for the ribs of the hand; then place upon the broken rib an elyptical piece according to the length of the rib, and slightly larger, then put under it the table I mentioned, and tighten the attachment; and if there are two or three, or more, break them, if on each rib you place an elyptical piece according to its size, wrapped in one linen sheet, and tighten the table under this piece; and stay positioned on the top of the table facing down towards the belly beneath it, so that it cuts well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things I've said about other injuries, once we have discussed them; and treat each case according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of nature breaks in a woman, if she lets it swell, then inclines her to the back part and is held from behind; fill the cavity that nature intended for the wound with cotton, and put also as much as there is. Then stand the woman upright, lift up her back slowly, and then let the cotton go until it reaches the entrance of nature, and carry along the bone with your hand; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and upon doing so, have her return to normal, like this for seven days or more: the break will be healed. If you see fit, take a bladder of goatskin and tie it to one end of a stick, and fill the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the stick until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will heal the break itself. Fill it with cotton, and leave like this for a few days, till it's healed properly.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand is broken, or in the case of a woman if it is fixed so as we have said in the hip bone; and these nearby breaks should not be hidden by someone who devotes their study and practice to it, and heed my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies in many positions the correct way to restore: therefore, understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an oxtail and fill it with the penis; then wrap it in bandages all around, and leave it for three days or as long thereafter, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, even if it's large, such as the bone of the rib or shoulder or resembling others, that it should be now cauterized, so that the cauterizations which we have mentioned testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, you should still apply vinegar to it, even if you don't have anything else. Proceed then to restore the break in the same hour or day, or at least wait for the pus from an abscess not to come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus from an abscess has come out, allow the restoration to continue for another day or two, until the pus subsides. Don't touch it at all on the third day or fourth day, as you might provoke a bad setback.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if you see the bone broken appearing on the part uncovered by the cut, it is necessary that you place your hands gently on it, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not appear for you to place evenly with your hands, then take this tool made of iron, which is about seven inches or six inches long, and its width should be according to the size of the wound; and it's necessary for the surgeon that he uses three or four of them, depending on what he needs for each cure of broken bones; and may be round and a little thick so that they do not bend under compression on your limb during surgery, and may be smooth in front, and thick at the center advancing, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche" because it means that the curved bones should be placed on the tip of the apparent bone; and it should be struck once, until it heals, and be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the tools cannot properly take hold of the bone, it means that you should copy the tip of the bone as long as the tools have the ability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone, as we have said, using an appropriate tool for this purpose, such as an incisor or saw, with your power; then cut that which is remaining in the hard and small scratches of the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the organs feel intense pain afterwards, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you manage to place it in its natural position, then soak the bandage in a black and stoptic wine, and properly do this especially if it's external; don't put any paste or other substance on the wound that might cause oiliness, which could lead to pus formation and decay. Then administer herbs after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, covering only the entire area according to the size of the wound. Be sure to watch carefully not to compress the wound with pressure; many times people have done this incorrectly, causing injury or even death at the wound site on subsequent occasions; and so the constraints should be softer and more soothing compared to other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that some accident might have occurred there, as we said earlier, and you find pain in your arm, then it doesn't suit to apply ointments; but wrap around, instead of ointments, hard cloths, and bind them tightly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is healing and the swelling has gone down, remove what you have applied with all the wine, and then apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as a tetraroma ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be braced in such a way that the joint moves slightly backwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot be joined back but allows movement of the joint, you should know that there are small bone fragments causing this pain, so it is necessary for you to treat the wound with traction, and remove all these worn-out pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the wound or any other manner of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what he instructed in his previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed in the body, such as in the case of the skull or shoulder blade, or other large bones, do not attempt to remove them because many die from it. Leave it until it heals naturally; perhaps it will heal within twenty days or thirty. Then treat the wound if you can. If you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The blows that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The blows come often after the healing of injuries, even especially when close to joints. It's a thing to see how the member's shape changes; and by chance can't perform its natural tasks on the member.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore when it comes to swellings: if you administer any stictching medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarsaparilla, senna, and the likes; or whatever among these things you choose, or all together, mix them with stictching wine or with enough egg or with garlic; and apply them on the swellings in poultices, bind them well, do not remove them by hand for days; then remove them, and start again another one until all the swellings are gone. Or you can bind it to a properly made piece of plaster; for the property of plaster is that it removes all swellings from the limbs. And if the swelling has turned hard like stone, as needing removal, if it is covered, cut away the excess and make its excess visible; or remove it with any barber until it's gone, then treat until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The member which becomes weak after confinement or imprisonment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breakage of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens due to various reasons: because it was bound too tightly and wasn't bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and couldn't come into alignment with the limb; or because of excessive swelling; or because of too large movements, not in their proper time; or because they have little blood in their body, so it's weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure involves having you eat the herbs, and make the body tender, until the healing spreads within him; then he should take baths and have fun and rest. After that, apply grease to the limb, so that the grease draws towards the major swelling, and washes it with cold water repeatedly, until the swelling aligns with the limb; and restore his natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is twisted after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if you break them open, even though the shape of the limb is distorted, it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those who say one should break the limb completely anew; many have done this in our land, and these methods are criticized, leading to great harms, perhaps even death. Nonetheless, when fractures and injuries are fresh, it's fitting that they be immersed in hot water or that medicinal plants like the leaves of basil, roots, and meadowsweet are cooked, such as with dyaquilon well made, and you use a musk paste from basil, mixed with fat from gelatine or oil of sassafras, and make a plaster out of it. Or you take greased figs, grind them with charcoal ash, and similar medications that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is the node removed by constantly rubbing it for a long period with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be a gentle movement of the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and stiff, like bone, and needs to be treated with iron, should it come to that point where the iron has to be applied up to the bone, gently incise through the thin opening; and apply cautery and careful study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to any, if it happens now to be properly returned without injury.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	And if you delay, the limbs will swell, and by chance you might put them in peril; for it is not right to move them when they are swollen: many times pus and other pains come about. Nonetheless, whenever this happens, have a surgeon look over the patient, then leave him alone until the abscess subsides; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as the treatment calls for in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters concerning shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat osseous at their joints and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the bottom, causing saliva from the mouth to leak out, unable to hold it, nor can they close their mouth, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When dislocations are small, they can return through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is whole and completed, you should reset it quickly, without hesitation; and do this while the ministers are cutting off the head of the sick person, and support one of her/his fingers under the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and the other hand should be out, to make them equal. Command the patient to soften their jaws, and move them in every direction.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he should gently place the bone until it returns to its place when it wakes up.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it is difficult, indeed if they are the two jaws together, so immerse them in hot water and oil, as long as you gently move them back; do not apply force during the return, just like we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well after being mollified, then place wet cloths as wads in a paste made from olive oil and beeswax, then bind it loosely with moist linen; let the patient lie on their back, and their limbs be between two cushions, so that they do not move nor to the right nor to the left, nor strain themselves at all, but should only eat light food until the pains are relieved, and the jaws are set; and then serve them what they wish lightly, and do not allow them to open their mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not naturally converted to their usual state, it leads to fevers that settle in, as well as abdominal distention, and sometimes vomiting of undigested food.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, death befalls the one who encounters this within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the strength
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot dislocate from within the continuous structure of it and from its bottom, and is dislocated only outside once, and one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on their back, and extends their arms; and then press the body into your palm shape, and it will return. Then apply a plaster and bind it, and tighten; and the thigh which faces the leg cannot dislocate; if not, should they dislocate once, you reset them to their place, as we have said; then apply the plaster and bind it, and tighten, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus similarly is brought back the shoulder blades when they are out of place due to their dislocation.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You should know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: first, it slips down to the armpit region; second, at the back part of the buttocks; and occasionally, above, which happens rarely; and it doesn't slip behind the shoulder blade or within due to nerves; and it gets repeatedly dislocated downwards towards the axilla area, even with those who have little flesh. For those who have a bit of muscle, it jumps out through its points and comes back in through its points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men due to impact or fracture, and inflames the shoulder in an abscess-like manner, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you must verify it, until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you are aware of the dislocations when it moves downward towards the axilla. You'll notice differences between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, finding a clear manifestation among them; in particular, there's a hollow at the top of the shoulder, from the armpit up to the collarbone, just like if it were an oes. The patient cannot bring his hand back under his nose or move it with any motion; similarly, if the dislocation occurs high up, it isn't hidden either, as you find it clearly at the collarbone; this method of dislocation can only be rectified when new, or when the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister raises his hand from the malady up, then places his fingers on the joint and lifts the joint upwards with force at the place; and the minister raises his hand and extends it upwards, placing him there; if he goes too quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it doesn't come so as we have said in a few days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and he should be treated with soothing and calming methods, such as decoctions of parsley and fenugreek and meadowsweet in water, and given to him; then wrap the patient on his back, and place a blanket of equal thickness under his buttocks, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the shoe on his heel, and firmly raise the head of the shoulder, pulling the hand towards it; and another helper should trim the head of the shoulder so that it doesn't move downwards; this shoulder returns immediately now, and if you see that you have successfully performed this method: then there must be someone present in your home who is larger than the patient; and stand upright facing the side, pushing the shoulder under the blanket with the patient's back, lift the blanket up so that the patient hangs at an angle; and another helper should pull the hand towards it downwards near the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, unable to lift anything heavy, and the dislocation returns right away.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And to reset it you can do it in other ways as well: and what you do is stick the long rod into the ground, so that the shoulder is also positioned like a dart, and not too large or too slippery; then place this over the patient but ensure there's grease underneath, and make sure the patient stays stationary for a long time with the rod; then extend their hand downwards from the other side in position, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it doesn't return through all these things that we've said, do this cure: take a torch of two arms wide and four inches thick, which has the head hollowed out so as to fit into the socket when inserted from below, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then bind the trunk with a cloth underneath to prevent it from rubbing against the affected area; place it on its back under the affected area; and extend your arms along the trunk up to its full length, bind the shoulder in place on the trunk, and position your hand's arm at its base; then place your arm on one thick stick of about the same width, and keep your hands down, leaving your body hanging from the other side: the joint will now return immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, however manner, that you must place a thread equal on the joint, then apply plaster covered in powder from the mill, along with incense and yolk of egg, over the entire shoulder and around it, then remove the plaster once the process is done, and re-tie the bandage on top of the plaster, and hold the hand near its neck, and let your hands stay like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary for him to eat a little, until the limbs are strengthened, because he will heal faster; and then increase his meals after five days or seven, and move them; and if it is firm and not softened, he will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joints have moved due to moisture or for some other reason that has caused this issue, it is necessary that you apply three cauteries to them, as was described earlier in our treatise on the use of cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't stay in place, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint would never settle back into its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs near the buttocks and breasts, or behind, is caused by pushing and stretching of hands, and it's administered elsewhere; treatment should be given as long as one remains healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there comes stiffness in the limb, and gradual movements later on, then they should use warm baths repeatedly until this stiffness disappears, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated at its peaks and returns there; it has been dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation cannot be remedied because you can see it clearly and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick to the healthy side with your hand, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the connection is uneven, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder to any extent.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it should be that you reset it in this manner as for pus wounds, because if pus wounds came about, there would be trouble in bringing them back; and by chance they cannot be brought back entirely, even when it is at the rear; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows: when it is such that one can return it to its position, you extend your hand of his two hands; and his arms are spread out, and his hands are turned towards the center according to the circumference of the elbow from inside, outside and underneath, and force the joint back into its place together or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And when there is a dislocation of the head, it returns whenever he doubles his hand over his own hand, and brings back the elbow that has been dislocated to the base of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it doesn't return to its original position, administer strong extension; and when you do so, extend the arm with both hands and stretch them outwards as far as possible, making sure not to move during this process. Then bend the arm in opposite directions, once having wrapped a double length of long and wide cloth around him. When you aim to connect the joint back onto your hand, anoint it with oil to soften the connection, then forcefully bring together the joint again until it begins to heal. Once healed, place it on a dry plaster bed covered with egg yolk, stretch it out carefully, and allow the arm to remain against the sick side for some days before removing the bandage.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, remove the bandage and leave it as is; and if you notice that the joint does not settle well, redo the plaster and the bandage, then let it be like this for a few days until it is firmly set; then remove the bandage.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if they feel the joint is twisted after returning it to its place, and it moves again, then bathe and scrub well afterwards, pressing until it is numb. Or you should apply butter on the joint for one day and one night, then wash with water; and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the butter back on, and then enter into the bath; repeat this process twice or three times until they are healed. And if you see fit, place moistened calf's fat heated with butter over it, and press it down; if it returns to its position again.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, then indeed it is well. If not, if the strain of plaster poultices for abscesses has relieved them, and leaves him so without needing to begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you can't leave him in place after some days, if the joint remains bent; and it does not harm him as long as his hands are immobilized, and cannot strain anything at all: then know that a nerve is cut, or an artery; if there's no other way to strain by cautery in this case, and by chance there's no other means.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in position, place it on the plaster as we have said, then apply pressure and leave it for five days, then remove it and let it be like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be moved well, and there is no break, with hot water grease, and rub it until it becomes clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part. dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	In the reduction of the heel, in the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When it is dislocated at the back of the heel or neck, or multiple are dislocated, if there's no treatment, because time quickens the disease.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot. Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those who have just given birth or been struck by objects or similar things, according to the old methods of treatment as described in lengthy texts, did not always derive great benefit from them; but I have summarized these instructions based on my intention and devised various tools for their application.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I state that when the foetus comes before the nipples, nothing is to be found; similarly, the one coming straight down to both sides, it can only be treated with what directly affects the back, as I say; and if the mother's body is extended over her belly evenly up to the first rib, and there is pressure from within her body against it, preventing any bruising; then stick a stake into the head in the ground forming soil, and another at the sides, and tie two strings under these stakes among the ribs near the muscles, and another at the hips, knees, and ankles; and two attendants should hold these strings, one by the head and the other by the sides, between the two stakes; they must be held tightly together, as we have said for the stake, and the mother should place her palms on the spine forming soil until she revives.

And if it doesn't recover from this treatment, take a board of three lengths long, and place it over the body. If the patient is on their side, put the patient under the board with their body against it, then position one end of the board so that the board touches the backside of the spine; set the middle of the board above the spine. Place their feet at either other end of the board and press firmly until they return to consciousness; if you see an improvement, do this on the elbow which turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And if you stick two thongs to the head of a patient's arm as long as your hand, and in front of their feet two others, with each thong having about three handbreadths between them; and place at each end a piece that has the elbow joint or turns correctly, firmly burying the ends of the thongs into the ground so they don't move; and between each pair of these two thongs, stick one turning thong, whose joints turn towards it; and in the two turning ones, insert little sticks about three handbreadths long to turn the elbows; then tie a link among them at the elbow towards the head, and another link towards the feet at the other elbow, and each of servants turns their elbow along its whole length, and masters make the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it's even, if you place desiccating plaster with plenty of egg whites, then apply ointment, and use an ash from a tablet of three inches long, that purifies the site of the cyst and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and instruct the patient in subtle nourishing techniques, until they are well; and if any sign appears during recovery, then you should administer softening medicines and soothing treatments, using the technique that we have discussed previously; and each time something is administered of powdered bread, and each time there's an appearance at the lower spine behind the back, suspect it might be dislocation; and it's the bone that's opening, so one must not presume: by chance it could cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You should know that the joints of the hip and the shoulder can only experience dislocations alone, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: within and outward, and in front and behind; it dislocates more inwardly and less forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is this: when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it's longer, and opens wider than the healthy leg at the knee joint; and the diseased knee cannot bend as far as the healthy one does; and there are abscesses bulging under those limbs because the heel of the leg has come to rest against them.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign for him who approaches fire, it is that such accidents are contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs for him who encounters ahead, it is that his leg must be well according to accomplishment; however, neither double its ankle without pain, and if one wants to make him move, he cannot beforehand, and he holds back his urine, and swells his foot, and when he walks, he does so on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs for him who encounters behind, it is that he cannot spread his ankle or double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and his foot becomes relaxed, and the head of the shoulder is in its place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The restoration of this illusion of dislocation is that you must understand that when dislocation has occurred and it remains according to its position, without any treatment, and there should not be any assumption made about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those where the dislocation is recent, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry you should return the joint, stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, no other treatment will be necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it doesn't return in this manner, then you should give strong assistance and hold the leg firmly with two hands or tie it tightly above the knee; and another assistant extends their hand over like this, so their palms are touching each other under the buttocks. Then they thrust their arms back up and down using a firm pull on the rope at the ankle; and another grabs the loop of the rope at the calf; and extend both upwards and downwards simultaneously until that point when the diseased limb is lifted off the ground all at once, and remains hanging for a time.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common among four similar situations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you should apply treatment according to its appearance. Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tie it in this way as we have said, then it's necessary that you tie both legs of the malady together with a strong band around their heels and knees, and make the leg on the malady extend more than two feet compared to the others; then hang him from his head with a pole, and raise his arms long above the ground; then command another person to hold the end of his leg, while other assistants hold onto him together, gripping in front of his leg, because it's returning to its position quickly now.

And if the dislocation is at the back, then it does not allow extending the patient backward or lifting them off the ground. de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint is dislocated in three ways: this means, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
